Two Claimants with Evidence: Judicial Decision
Chapter opening: ruling on two claimants with evidence over an item in third party possession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when two claimants both present evidence for an item in a third party's possession and identify that the judge must make a decision between them.

Core Idea
Equal proof from both claimants leads to judicial decision, not automatic division.

This lesson introduces a foundational ruling in Hanafi judicial procedure (qada). When two people each claim ownership of the same physical item held by a third party, and both produce evidence, the judge does not automatically award the item to either or divide it. Instead, the judge must render a judgment between them, which may involve further scrutiny or equal division depending on the strength of evidence. This rule underscores the role of the judge in resolving competing claims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize that two claimants are both asserting ownership of a specific tangible item ('ayn) that is currently in the possession of a third person. The third party is not a claimant but a holder.
The item must be a specific physical object ('ayn), not a debt or benefit.
2
Note the evidential condition
Both claimants have established evidence (bayyinah) – typically witness testimony – proving their ownership. The text assumes both have equally valid proof.
If only one had evidence, the ruling would differ (the one with evidence prevails).
3
Apply the judicial outcome
The judge must make a decision between them (faysal baynahuma). This does not automatically mean the item is divided; the judge may investigate further, consider quality of evidence, or divide if evidence is equal.
In Hanafi fiqh, if evidence is equal and both are reliable, the item is divided equally between the two claimants.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ ما يدعيه الرجلان دو آدمیوں نے دعوی کیا ایک عین (چیز) کا جو تیسرے کے قبضہ میں ہے ان میں سے ہر ایک کہتا ہے کہ یہ میری ہے اور دونوں نے بینہ قائم کر دیئے تو دونوں کے درمیان فیصلہ کیا جائے گا
Chapter on what two men claim. Two men claimed an 'ayn (a thing) which is in the possession of a third, each of them says it is mine, and both established evidence, so judgment will be made between them.
Source pages p. 4

Commentary
This passage introduces a chapter from Ashraf al-Hidayah on disputes where two claimants both claim ownership of a specific item (عين) that is in the possession of a third person. The ruling given is that if both claimants produce evidence (بيّنة) of ownership, the judge should make a decision between them (i.e., possibly divide the item or rule in favor of one based on strength of evidence). The text does not specify the basis of judgment, but in Hanafi fiqh, if both have equal evidence, the item is divided between them. This is a procedural ruling in the chapter of judicial decisions (qada).

Key Terms
عین ('ayn): A specific, tangible property (as opposed to debt or benefit). In this ruling, it refers to a physical object that is the subject of the claim.
بینہ (bayyinah): Evidence, typically testimony of witnesses. In this context, it means both claimants produced witnesses or proof of ownership.
قبضہ (qabdah): Possession. The third party has actual control or custody over the item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Two claimants both present witnesses for the same item in a third party's possession. According to the Hanafi ruling, what must the judge do?
A) Give the item to the third party
B) Reject both claims due to conflict
C) Make a decision between the two claimants
D) Award the item to the first claimant

Key Takeaway
When two claimants both have evidence for an item held by a third party, the judge must render a decision between them.

Rulings on Competing Claims with Evidence
Fihrist entry summarizing rulings on competing claims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rules for resolving competing claims when both parties present evidence, and identify which party is preferred based on the type and strength of proof.

Core Idea
When both claimants have evidence, the judge decides by strength of proof—dates, possession, and birth evidence all affect preference.

This passage from the Hidayah fihrist summarizes key rulings in qada for situations where two men claim the same item, marriage, or animal. Each scenario tests the principle that evidence (bayyinah) must be evaluated by its strength, not just its presence. These rulings form the foundation for Hanafi judicial practice in cases of competing claims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and parties
Determine what is being claimed (item, marriage, animal) and who the claimants are (possessor, non-possessor, buyer, etc.).
2
Note the type of evidence each presents
Look for whether each party offers witnesses, possession, a date, or evidence of birth. The specific combination triggers different preference rules.
3
Apply the preference rule
Based on the scenario, apply the Hanafi rule: earlier date, possession, birth evidence, or purchase evidence may give priority.
Key: possession gives an advantage, but birth evidence beats ownership evidence.
4
Evaluate witness count
If multiple witnesses are presented, the number does not decide; strength of evidence (e.g., consistency, credibility) determines preference.
The passage explicitly states: preference is not by multiplicity but by strength of action.
5
Extract the general principle
The common thread: evidence is evaluated by its intrinsic strength, not by quantity or mere presence. The judge must weigh factors like date, possession, and birth.
This principle guides Hanafi qada in all property and personal status claims.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بابُ ما يدعيه الرجلان
دو آدمیوں نے دعوی کیا ایک عین (چیز) کا جو تیسرے کے قبضہ میں ہے ان میں سے ہر ایک کہتا ہے کہ یہ میری ہے اور دونوں نے مبینہ قائم کر دیئے تو دونوں کے درمیان فیصلہ کیا جائے گا
دو آدمیوں نے ایک عورت سے نکاح کا دعویٰ کیا اور دونوں نے گواہ قائم کر دیئے تو بینہ کی وجہ سے کسی ایک کے لئے فیصال نہیں کیا جائے گا اگر قاضی نے دونوں کے درمیان غلام کے نصف نصف ہونے کا فیصلہ کر دیا پھر ایک نے کہا کہ میں نصف نہیں لینا چاہتا تو دوسرے کے لئے پورا غلام لینے کا اختیار نہیں ہوگا
ایک نے خریدنے کا اور دوسرے نے صبر مع القبض کا دعویٰ کیا اور دونوں نے مدینہ قائم کر دیئے اور تاریخ کسی کے پاس نہیں تو خریدار اولی ہے اگر دو غیر قابضوں نے ہینہ قائم کئے ملک اور تاریخ پر تو سابق تاریخ والا اوٹی ہے غیر قابض نے ہینہ قائم کئے ملک مورخ پر اور قبضہ والے نے تقدیر تاریخ پر مبینہ قائم کئے تو قابض اولی ہے قابض اور غیر قابض دونوں نے ہینہ قائم کئے پیدائش پر تو قابض اولی ہے ہر ایک نے ملک حاصل کی کسی شخص سے اور اسکی اپنے پاس پیدائش پر گواہ پیش کئے تو اپنے قبضہ میں پیدا ہونے پر گواہ قائم کرنے کی طرح ہے۔ ایک نے ملک پر اور دوسرے نے پیدائش پر گواہ قائم کئے تو پیدائش والا اولی ہے ہر ایک نے دوسرے سے خریدنے پر گواہ قائم کئے اور تاریخ کسی کے پاس نہیں تو گواہ ساقط ہوں گے اور مکان قابض کے قبضہ میں چھوڑ دیا جائے گا دو مدعیوں میں سے ایک نے دو اور دوسرے نے چار گواہ پیش کئے تو سب برابر ہیں ترجیح کثرت علل سے نہیں قوت عمل سے ہوتی ہے ) دو آدمیوں نے جھگڑا کیا ایک چوپایہ کے بارے میں اور ہر ایک نے گواہ قائم کر دیئے کہ وہ میرے ہاں پیدا ہوا ہے اور دونوں نے تاریخ ذکر کی اور جانور کی عمر کسی ایک کی تاریخ کے مطابق ہے تو وہی اولی ہے
Chapter on what two men claim. Two men claimed a specific item that is in the possession of a third, each saying it is mine, and both presented evidence, then judgment will be made between them. Two men claimed marriage to a woman and both presented witnesses, then due to the testimony, judgment will not be made for either; if the judge decreed that the slave is half-half between them, then one said he does not want the half, the other will not have the option to take the whole slave. One claimed purchase and the other claimed possession with receipt, and both presented evidence and no one has a date, then the buyer is preferred; if two non-possessors presented evidence on ownership and date, then the one with the earlier date is preferred; a non-possessor presented evidence on ownership with date and the possessor presented evidence on the date of possession, then the possessor is preferred; both possessor and non-possessor presented evidence on birth, then the possessor is preferred; each claimed ownership from a person and presented witnesses on its birth with him, it is like presenting witnesses on its birth in his possession. One presented evidence on ownership and the other on birth, then the one with birth is preferred. Each presented evidence on purchasing from the other and no one has a date, then the evidence is invalid and the house will be left in the possession of the possessor. Among two claimants, one presented two witnesses and the other four, all are equal; preference is not due to multiplicity of causes but due to strength of action. Two men disputed about an animal and each presented witnesses that it was born with him, and both mentioned dates, and the age of the animal corresponds to the date of one of them, then that one is preferred.
Source pages p. 4

Commentary
This passage is a fihrist (table of contents) entry summarizing key rulings from the chapter on claims of two men. It covers various scenarios: when two claimants both present evidence for the same item, the judge decides between them. In marriage claims, testimony does not give preference. When one claims purchase and the other possession, the buyer is preferred if no dates. When both have dates, the earlier date is preferred. If one has evidence of ownership and the other of birth, birth evidence is preferred. The passage also states that the number of witnesses does not outweigh the strength of evidence. These are foundational rules for qada' (judicial proceedings) in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
بینہ (bayyinah): Evidence or testimony presented in court, typically by witnesses.
اولی (awla): Preferred or having priority in judicial decision.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If two claimants present evidence for ownership of an item, but one has an earlier date and the other has no date, who is preferred?
A) The one with the earlier date
B) The one with more witnesses
C) The possessor
D) The judge declares the item for the third party

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi qada, when both claimants present evidence, the judge must evaluate the strength of the proof—by date, possession, birth, or purchase—rather than the number of witnesses.

Dispute over Hands: Hanafi Rules of Possession
Fihrist entry on disputes based on physical control

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state and apply the Hanafi evidential rules for resolving disputes over physical possession in five specific scenarios.

Core Idea
Physical possession (yad) creates a presumption of ownership, but its weight varies by scenario.

This fihrist entry summarizes key rulings from the chapter on disputes over hands (al-tanazu' bi'l-aydi). These rules guide a Hanafi judge in determining ownership when physical control is contested. They reflect the principle that possession is a strong, but not absolute, indicator, with specific exceptions and refinements based on the nature of control.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nature of possession
Determine whether each party has direct physical control (riding, holding reins, sitting) or constructive possession (structural attachment, rooms).
Direct control often gives a stronger claim.
2
Apply the default rule of stronger control
The party with more direct or integral control is preferred. For example, the rider over the rein-holder, and the one with more beams over the one with fewer.
This is a qadāʾī presumption, not absolute ownership proof.
3
Apply the exception for dependent testimony
When a child in possession can express himself and declares his own status (e.g., free), his statement is accepted over the possessor's claim.
This is an exception to the general rule that minors cannot testify.
4
Apply rules for fixtures and structures
Attachments that are essential to the structure (like beams) shift ownership presumptions; non-essential ones (doors, windows) do not. A threshold of three beams decides wall ownership.
These rules reflect the principle that possession is evidenced by integral, not incidental, control.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في التنازع بالايدى
دو آدمیوں نے ایک چوپایہ کے بارے میں جھگڑا کیا ایک راکب ہے اور دوسرا اس کی لگام تھامے ہوئے ہے تو را کب اوٹی ہے بچہ کسی کے قبضہ میں ہو اور وہ اپنی ذات سے تعبیر کر سکتا ہے اس نے کہا میں آزاد ہوں تو اس بچہ کا قول معتبر ہوگا کسی کی دیوار پر دوسرے کا شہتیر یا اس کی عمارت متصل ہے اور اس پر دوسرے کی دردوک ہے تو دیوار، شبیر اتصال والے کا ہے اور در دوک کچھ نہیں اگر ایک کی کڑیاں تین سے کم ہیں تو دیوار تین والے کی ہوگی اور دوسرے کے لئے کڑیاں رکھنے کی جگہ ہوگی ایک کے قبضہ میں گھر کے دس کمرے اور دوسرے کے قبضہ میں ایک کمرہ ہے محن دونوں کے درمیان نصف نصف ہو گا اور اس کے استعمال میں دونوں برابر ہیں
Section on dispute over hands. Two men disputed about an animal, one is a rider and the other holding its reins, then the rider is preferred. If a child is in someone's possession and he can express himself, and he says 'I am free', then his statement is credible. On someone's wall, another has a beam or his building is attached, and on it the other has a door and a window, then the wall belongs to the one with the beam attached, and the door and window are nothing. If one has fewer than three beams, then the wall belongs to the one with three, and the other will have a place to put beams. One has possession of ten rooms of a house and the other has possession of one room, then the work (or the house?) will be half-half between them, and they are equal in its use.
Source pages p. 4

Commentary
This fihrist entry summarizes rulings from the section on disputes based on physical control (yad). The rider is preferred over the one holding the reins because he has greater control. A child's statement about freedom is accepted if he can express himself. In disputes over walls and beams, the one with the attached beam has ownership of the wall; beams less than three do not shift ownership. If one person possesses ten rooms and another one room, they share the house equally (half-half) and use it equally. These rules reflect Hanafi principles of possession as evidence of ownership.

Key Terms
قبضہ (qabdah): Physical possession or control over an item.
راکب (rakib): Rider of an animal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The rider
B) The one holding the reins
C) They split equally
D) The judge takes the animal

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi qada, the nature and strength of physical possession determines ownership in disputes, with specific rules for riders, children, and structural attachments.

Liability in Disputed Deposit vs Usurpation
Ruling on iqrar of deposit and usurpation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between two scenarios of iqrar regarding wadi'ah and ghasb, and apply the Hanafi ruling on liability based on who admits what.

Core Idea
Liability depends on whether the confessor admits a contract (wadi'ah) or a tort (ghasb).

When two people dispute whether the possession of property was a deposit (wadi'ah) or usurpation (ghasb), the ruling on liability hinges on whose statement is accepted. This passage from Al-Hidayah presents two scenarios and explains the underlying reasoning through qiyas. Understanding this distinction is crucial for judges (qadi) and those involved in property disputes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Read the first two sentences: one where the depositee says he took as deposit and the owner says it was usurpation, and the second where the depositee says the owner gave as deposit and the owner denies. Note the different outcomes.
The key is who is the confessor (muqir) and what he admits.
2
Determine the ruling for each scenario
In the first scenario, the person who took the property (the depositee) is liable (damana). In the second, he is not liable. State these rulings clearly.
Liability = guarantee of the property value.
3
Analyse the reason for the difference
The passage gives a 'wajh farq' using an analogy: if A says he took a deposit from C, and C claims it as his own, C gets the property. This shows that the person's own admission determines the nature. Apply this to the scenarios.
The analogy illustrates that acceptance of the claim depends on consistency with one's own statement.
4
Extract the legal principle
The underlying principle is that if a person admits taking property but claims it was as a trust (wadi'ah), and the owner denies the trust, the taker is liable because his admission of receipt coupled with a claim of a contract that is denied makes him a wrongful possessor (ghasb by his own words). If the taker claims the owner gave as deposit and the owner denies, the taker is not liable because the owner's denial of the contract leaves the taker as a thief, but the taker's statement is not an admission against himself.
This is a form of istihsan or talil based on the nature of the admissions.
5
Apply to a modern case
Consider a case where A leaves a laptop with B, and later B says it was a gift, A says it was a loan. Using the same logic, determine who is liable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ایک شخص نے دوسرے کو کہا میں نے تجھ سے ہزار درہم ودیعت لئے تھے وہ تلف ہو گئے ہیں۔ اس نے کہا نہیں تم نے بطور غصب کے لئے تھے تو مقرضا من ہو گا اگر مقر نے کہا کہ تم نے مجھے ودیعت دیئے تھے اس نے کہا نہیں تم نے غصب کئے تھے تو مقر ضامن نہ ہوگا ۔ وجہ فرق اگر کہا کہ یہ ہزار میرے فلاں کے پاس ودیعت تھے وہ میں نے لے لئے فلاں نے کہا وہ تو میرے ہیں تو فلاں لے لے گا
A person said to another: 'I took one thousand dirhams as deposit (wadi'ah) from you, and they were lost.' The other said: 'No, you took them as usurpation (ghasb).' Then the depositor will be the guarantor. If the confessor said: 'You gave me as deposit,' and the other said: 'No, you usurped them,' then the confessor will not be liable. The reason for the difference: If he said, 'This thousand was a deposit with so-and-so, I took them,' and so-and-so said, 'They are mine,' then so-and-so will take them.
Source pages p. 6

Commentary
This passage explains the rulings when two parties dispute the nature of possession: deposit (wadi'ah) or usurpation (ghasb). The key is whose statement is accepted. If A says he took as deposit and B says it was ghasb, then A is liable (as the depositee who lost the deposit). But if A says B gave as deposit and B denies, then A is not liable because the deposit requires a contract which B denies. The 'وجہ فرق' gives an analogy: if A says he took a deposit from C, and C claims it as his own, then C takes the property, showing that the person's own admission determines the nature.

Key Terms
ودیعت (wadīʿa): A deposit; property left with someone for safekeeping without compensation.
غصب (ghaṣb): Usurpation; wrongful possession of someone else's property without right.
اقرار (iqrār): Confession or admission against oneself in legal matters.
ضامن (ḍāmin): Guarantor or liable party; one who must compensate for loss.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the second scenario of the passage, the confessor says 'You gave me as deposit,' and the other says 'No, you usurped them.' What is the ruling?
A) The confessor is liable
B) The confessor is not liable
C) Both are liable
D) The owner is liable

Key Takeaway
In disputes over possession, the Hanafi school distinguishes liability based on whether the confessor admits taking the property or merely claims a contract that the other denies.

Istihsan in Iqrar: Accepting the Possessor's Word
Ruling on istihsan in iqrar disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule when a confessor disputes the worker's claim and explain why istihsan gives preference to the possessor.

Core Idea
In disputes over improvements, the possessor's word prevails by istihsan.

The text presents a scenario where a person confesses that another cultivated, built, or planted on his land, but then disputes ownership, claiming it was done as a favour or for wages. The question arises: whose statement is believed? Hanafi fiqh applies istihsan to favour the possessor, based on the strength of possession. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the operative rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and dispute
Read the passage carefully. The confessor admits the work but denies the worker's ownership. The worker claims the improvements belong to him. The key is that the property is in the confessor's possession.
Possession is the central fact.
2
Recognize the default rule (qiyas) and the istihsan exception
Under strict qiyas, the confessor's admission might be taken as evidence for the worker, but istihsan overrides this because possession provides stronger evidence of ownership.
Istihsan is not arbitrary; it is based on a stronger proof.
3
Understand the basis for istihsan
The principle 'al-ashbah yurattu' (the apparent is followed) means the apparent owner (possessor) is believed. The possessor's word is preferred because it aligns with the visible reality.
This is a well-known Hanafi maxim.
4
Note the mufta bihi ruling
The confessor's statement is accepted with oath. The worker must bring proof if he claims ownership.
This is from Zahir al-Riwayah.
5
Compare cross-madhhab differences
The Shafi'i school may require hearing from the worker because the admission creates a presumption. The Hanafi view prioritizes possession.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجه استحسان اقرار کیا کہ فلاں نے اس زمین میں کاشت کی یا اس دار میں عمارت بنائی یا انگور کے باغ میں پودے لگائے اور یہ سب مقر کے قبضہ میں ہے پھر فلاں نے ان کا دعویٰ کیا مقر نے کہا نہیں یہ تو میرے ہین میں نے تجھ سے صرف استعانت لی تھی ہو تو نے کر دی یا تو نے مزدوری پر کام کیا تو کس کا قول معتبر ہوگا
The reason for istihsan: He confessed that so-and-so cultivated in this land, or built a building in this house, or planted saplings in a vineyard, and all this is in the possession of the confessor. Then so-and-so claimed them. The confessor said: 'No, they are mine. I only sought help from you, and you did it,' or 'You worked for wages.' Then whose statement will be trusted?
Source pages p. 6

Commentary
This passage discusses the principle of istihsan in the context of iqrar. The scenario: a person confesses that another performed acts like cultivation, building, or planting on property that the confessor possesses. When the worker claims ownership of the improvements or the property, the confessor denies and says the worker did it as a helper or for hire. The question is whose word is accepted. The principle of istihsan (juristic preference) would give preference to the possessor (confessor) because the default is that the property belongs to him. The worker must prove his claim. This is contrary to qiyas which might require the confessor to prove, but istihsan protects ownership.

Key Terms
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference; deviating from qiyas for a stronger reason.
اقرار (iqrār): Confession; acknowledgment of a fact or right.
قیاس (qiyās): Analogical deduction; extending a ruling from an original case to a new case based on shared cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Qada — Judiciary

Dispute Between Two Claimants: Evidence and Equal Division (Hanafi vs. Shafi'i)
Explains Hanafi ruling and proof for dividing the item equally between two claimants with evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a dispute between two claimants with evidence and explain why the Hanafi school divides the item equally, citing the hadith of Tamim ibn Tarafa and the abrogation of the hadith of lots.

Core Idea
When both claimants present evidence, the item is divided equally—both testimonies can be true if based on different grounds.

This passage addresses a classic juridical problem: two individuals each claim ownership of a single item held by a third party, and both present witnesses. The Hanafi school holds that the item is divided equally between them, while Imam al-Shafi'i held two differing opinions—either the testimonies cancel each other out or lots are cast. Understanding the Hanafi reasoning requires careful analysis of the proofs and the principle that testimony can be valid from different perspectives.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Identify what the Hanafi school rules: the item is divided equally (tansif) between the two claimants.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i has two opinions: either the testimonies invalidate each other (tahatur) or lots are cast (qur'a).
The Shafi'i view is based on the impossibility of two full ownerships.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Shafi'i evidence: the hadith of lots where the Prophet cast lots, and the logical argument that one witness set must be false.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is twofold: (a) the hadith of lots is abrogated (mansukh) by the later hadith of equal division, and (b) both testimonies can be valid if one is based on a cause of ownership and the other on possession.
Thus both testimonies are acted upon as far as possible.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafi judges order the item split equally; Shafi'i judges either dismiss both claims or resort to lots.
The Hanafi ruling is operative (mufta bihi) in Hanafi jurisdictions.

بَابُ ما يدعيه الرجلان ترجمہ یہ باب دو شخصوں کے دعوئی کے بیان میں ہے دو آدمیوں نے دعویٰ کیا ایک عین (چیز) کا جو تیسرے کے قبضہ میں ہے ان میں سے ہر ایک کہتا ہے کہ یہ میری ہے اور دونوں نے بینہ قائم کر دیئے تو دونوں کے درمیان فیصلہ کیا جائے گا قَالَ وَإِذَا ادَّعَى اثْنَانِ عَيْنًا فِي يَدِ آخَرَ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا يَزْعَمُ أَنَّهَا لَهُ وَأَقَامَا الْبَيِّنَةَ قُضِيَ بِهَا بَيْنَهُمَا وَقَالَ تَمِيمِ بْنِ طَرْفَةَ أَنَّ رَجُلَيْنِ اخْتَصَمَا إِلَى رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فِي نَاقَةٍ وَأَقَامَ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِّنْهُمَا بَيْنَةً فَقَضَى بَيْنَهُمَا بِهَا نِصْفَيْنِ وَحَدِيثُ الْقُرْعَةِ كَانَ فِي ابْتِدَاءِ الْإِسْلَامِ ثُمَّ نُسِخَ وَلاَنَّ الْمُطْلَقَ لِلشَّهَادَةِ فِي حَقَ كُلَّ وَاحِدٍ مِّنْهُمَا مُحْتَمَلُ الْوُجُودِ بِأَنْ يَعْتِمَدَ اَحَدُهُمَا سَبَبَ الْمِلْكِ وَالْآخَرُ الْيَدَ فَصَحَتِ الشَّهَادَتَان فَيَجِبُ الْعَمَلُ بِهِمَا مَا اَمْكَنَ وَقَدْ أَمْكَنَ بِالتَّنْصِيْفِ إِذِ الْمَحْلُ يَقْبَلُهُ وَإِنَّمَا يَنْصَفُ لِإِسْتَوَانِهِمَا فِي سَبَبَ الْإِسْتِحْقَاقِ ترجمہ دعویٰ کیا دو نے ایک خاص چیز کا جو تیسرے کے قبضہ میں ہے اور ان میں سے ہر ایک کہتا ہے کہ یہ چیز میری ہے اور دونوں نے ہینہ قائم کر دیا تو فیصلہ ہوگا کہ وہ ان دونوں میں مساوی ہے۔ امام شافعی نے ایک قول میں کہا کہ دونوں ہیتہ ساقط ہوں گے۔ اور ایک قول میں کہا: کہ ان میں قرعہ اندازی کی جائے گی۔ اس لئے کہ ایک ہینہ یقینا کا ذب ہے۔ کل چیز میں بحالت واحدہ اجتماع ملکین محال ہونے کی وجہ سے اور جھوٹے پینہ کی تمیز متعذر ہوگئی تو دونوں ساقط ہو جائیں گے یا قرعہ کی طرف رجوع کیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ایسے معاملہ میں قرعہ ڈالا اور فرمایا: الہی ان میں تو ہی حاکم ہے۔ ہماری دلیل حدیث تمیم بن طرفہ ہے کہ دو شخصوں نے حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کے حضور میں ایک اونٹنی کی بابت جھگڑا کیا اور دونوں نے ہینہ قائم کر دیا تو آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے دونوں میں نصفا نصف ہونے کا حکم فرمایا اور حدیث قرعہ ابتداء اسلام میں تھی پھر منسوخ ہو گئی۔ اور اس لئے کہ فریقین میں سے ہر ایک کے حق میں مجیز شہادت محتمل الوجود ہے۔ بایں طور کہ ایک فریق نے سبپ ملک پر اور دوسرے نے قبضہ پر اعتماد کیا ہو۔ پس دونوں گواہیاں صحیح ہوئیں تو جہاں تک ممکن ہے دونوں پر عمل ضروری ہے اور یہاں بطریق تنصیف عمل ممکن ہے۔ کیونکہ محل قابل تنصیف ہے۔ اور تنصیف اسی لئے ہوئی ہے کہ سبب استحقاق میں دونوں برابر ہیں۔ تشریح قولہ باب ایک شخص کے دعوئی کے احکام سے فراغت کے بعد دو شخصوں کے دعوئی کے احکام بیان کر رہے ہیں ۔ لان المثنی بعد الواحد (غايه)
Chapter of What Two Men Claim. Explanation: This chapter is about the claims of two persons. Two men claimed a specific item that is in the possession of a third, each saying it is his, and both presented evidence. Then judgment is given that it is between them (divided equally). He said: When two claim an item in the hand of another, each claiming it is his, and they present evidence, judgment is given that it is between them. Al-Shafi'i said in one opinion: their evidence is invalid; and in another opinion: lots are cast between them, because one of the two pieces of evidence is certainly false, since it is impossible for two ownerships to combine in the whole in one situation. And discrimination has become impossible, so either they invalidate each other or recourse is made to lots, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) cast lots in such a case and said: 'O Allah, You are the Judge between them.' Our proof is the hadith of Tamim ibn Tarafa that two men disputed before the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) concerning a she-camel, and each presented evidence, so he judged it between them in half. And the hadith of lots was in early Islam, then it was abrogated. And because the absolutely given for testimony is possibly existent in the right of each of them, in that one relied on the cause of ownership and the other on possession, so both testimonies are valid; so it is obligatory to act on them as far as possible, and it is possible by halving, since the subject accepts it. And it is halved because they are equal in the cause of entitlement. Translation: Two claimed a specific item in the possession of a third, each saying it is his, and both presented evidence, then the judgment is that it is equal between them. Imam Shafi'i said in one opinion: both pieces of evidence are invalid. And in another opinion: lots are cast between them. Because one evidence is certainly false, due to impossibility of two ownerships combining in the whole at one time, and discrimination of the false evidence is impossible, so both fall, or recourse is to lots. Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) cast lots in such a case and said: 'O Allah, You are the Judge between them.' Our proof is the hadith of Tamim ibn Tarafa: two men disputed before the Prophet (peace be upon him) about a she-camel and each presented evidence, so he ordered it to be divided between them in half. And the hadith of lots was in early Islam, then abrogated. And because the possibility of testimony is existent for each party, in that one relied on the cause of ownership and the other on possession, so both testimonies are valid; so it is necessary to act on both as much as possible, and it is possible by halving, because the subject accepts halving. And halving is done because they are equal in the cause of entitlement. Explanation: After completing the rulings of one claimant, the rulings of two claimants are being explained, because the dual follows the singular.
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage is a detailed legal dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding a case where two claimants both present evidence of ownership over an item held by a third party. The Hanafi position, as stated by the author, is that the item is divided equally between the two claimants. This ruling is based on the hadith of Tamim ibn Tarafa, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) divided a she-camel between two disputants who both had evidence. The Hanafis argue that both testimonies are potentially valid—one may be based on a cause of ownership (e.g., purchase) and the other on possession—so both must be acted upon as far as possible. Since the item can be divided, the ruling is tasnif (halving). Imam al-Shafi'i, on the other hand, held two views: either the evidences invalidate each other (tahatur) or lots are cast (qur'a), because one evidence must be false since two full ownerships cannot coexist. The Hanafi response is that the hadith of lots from the Prophet was abrogated, and the later practice of division is the final ruling. The passage concludes with a brief explanatory note that after discussing a single claimant, the chapter moves to two claimants.

Key Terms
بینة (baiyina): Legal evidence, typically testimony of two witnesses or other proof accepted in court.
قرعة (qur'a): Lots; a method of decision when evidence is inconclusive, used in some schools.
تنصیف (tansif): Halving; dividing the disputed item equally between the two claimants.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling when two claimants both present evidence of ownership over an item in a third party's possession?
A) The evidence of both is invalid
B) Lots are cast to decide
C) The item is divided equally between them
D) The item is given to the third party

Key Takeaway
When both claimants present evidence, the Hanafi school divides the item equally because both testimonies can be true and the hadith of lots is abrogated.

Ruling When Two Claimants Present Evidence for an Item in a Third Party's Possession
Inter-madhhab dispute on equal division of a disputed item

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling of equal division, explain the Shafi'i objection, and reproduce the Hanafi response with dalil.

Core Idea
When two claimants present evidence, the Hanafi school divides the item equally — both testimonies can be true.

This passage presents a classic inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. Two claimants each produce evidence to ownership of an item in a third party's possession. The Hanafi ruling, grounded in a prophetic hadith and rational analysis, orders equal division. The Shafi'i school objects on the basis that one evidence must be false. By the end of this lesson, you will understand the proofs and counter-arguments that underpin this difference.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the judge should do according to the Hanafi school when both claimants present evidence.
The ruling is found in the opening sentence: 'qudiya biha baynahuma' – judged between them equally.
2
Identify the Shafi'i positions
Note the two opinions attributed to Imam al-Shafi'i: tahatur (both claims dropped) or qur'ah (casting lots).
These are based on the impossibility of two ownerships coexisting.
3
Examine the Shafi'i proof
Understand the Shafi'i argument: one evidence must be false because two separate owners cannot own the same whole item simultaneously.
They rely on a hadith where the Prophet cast lots and said 'Allahumma anta al-hakam baynahuma'.
4
Analyse the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi school uses the hadith of Tamim ibn Tarafah where the Prophet divided the she-camel in half. They also argue the casting lots hadith is abrogated.
Additionally, rational: one claimant may rely on a cause (like purchase) and the other on possession (like gift), both valid.
5
Derive the practical consequence
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf: in the Hanafi school the item is shared; in Shafi'i it either stays with the possessor or is awarded to the winner of the lot.
This difference affects how judges resolve property disputes.

Source Text

بَابُ ما يدعيه الرجلان
قَالَ وَإِذَا ادَّعَى اثْنَانِ عَيْنًا فِي يَدِ آخَرَ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا يَزْعَمُ أَنَّهَا لَهُ وَأَقَامَا الْبَيِّنَةَ قُضِيَ بِهَا بَيْنَهُمَا وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ فِي قَوْلٍ يَتَهَاتَرَانِ وَفِي قَوْلٍ يُقْرَعُ بَيْنَهُمَا لِأَنَّ إِحْدَى الْبَيِّنَتَيْنِ كَاذِبَةٌ بِيَقِينٍ لِاسْتِحَالَةِ اجْتِمَاعِ الْمِلْكَيْنِ فِي الْكُلِّ فِي حَالَةٍ وَاحِدَةٍ وَقَدْ تَعَذَّرَ التَّمْيِيزُ فَيَتَهَاتَرَانِ أَوْ يُصَارُ إِلَى الْقُرْعَةِ لِأَنَّ النَّبِيَّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ أَقْرَعَ فِيهِ وَقَالَ اللَّهُمَّ أَنْتَ الْحَكَمُ بَيْنَهُمَا وَلَنَا حَدِيثُ تَمِيمِ بْنِ طَرْفَةَ أَنَّ رَجُلَيْنِ اخْتَصَمَا إِلَى رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فِي نَاقَةٍ وَأَقَامَ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا بَيْنَةً فَقَضَى بَيْنَهُمَا بِهَا نِصْفَيْنِ وَحَدِيثُ الْقُرْعَةِ كَانَ فِي ابْتِدَاءِ الْإِسْلَامِ ثُمَّ نُسِخَ وَلِأَنَّ الْمُطْلَقَ لِلشَّهَادَةِ فِي حَقِّ كُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا مُحْتَمَلُ الْوُجُودِ بِأَنْ يَعْتَمِدَ أَحَدُهُمَا سَبَبَ الْمِلْكِ وَالْآخَرُ الْيَدَ فَصَحَّتِ الشَّهَادَتَانِ فَيَجِبُ الْعَمَلُ بِهِمَا مَا أَمْكَنَ وَقَدْ أَمْكَنَ بِالتَّنْصِيفِ إِذِ الْمَحَلُّ يَقْبَلُهُ وَإِنَّمَا يُنَصَّفُ لِاسْتِوَائِهِمَا فِي سَبَبِ الِاسْتِحْقَاقِ
Chapter of what two men claim. He said: And when two men claim a specific thing in the hand of another, each of them asserting that it is his, and they both produce evidence, then judgment is given for it between them equally. And al-Shafi'i said in one opinion: they both drop (their claims), and in another opinion: lots are cast between them, because one of the two evidences is certainly false, due to the impossibility of two ownerships being combined in the whole in one situation, and distinction has become impossible, so they both drop or recourse is made to casting lots, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) cast lots in it and said: 'O Allah, You are the Judge between them.' And we have the hadith of Tamim ibn Tarafah that two men disputed before the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) concerning a she-camel, and each of them produced evidence, so he judged between them by dividing it into halves. And the hadith of casting lots was in the beginning of Islam, then it was abrogated. And because the basis for testimony concerning each of them is possible of existence, in that one of them relies on a cause of ownership and the other on possession, so both testimonies are valid, and it is obligatory to act upon both as much as possible, and it is possible by division into halves, since the place accepts it, and it is divided into halves only because they are equal in the cause of entitlement.
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding two claimants who both produce evidence for an item in a third party's possession. The Hanafi position, as stated in the matn, is that the item is divided equally between them. The Shafi'i has two opinions: either both claims are dropped (tahatur) or lots are cast (qur'ah). Their proof is that one evidence must be false because two ownerships cannot coexist in the same item at the same time, and since it's impossible to distinguish, both evidences are invalidated. Alternatively, they rely on a hadith where the Prophet (ﷺ) cast lots in such a case. The Hanafi response is based on the hadith of Tamim ibn Tarafah where the Prophet divided the disputed camel. They argue that the hadith of casting lots was abrogated. Additionally, rationally, it is possible that both testimonies are correct—one based on a cause of ownership (e.g., purchase) and the other on possession (e.g., gift)—so both testimonies are valid and must be acted upon. Since the item can be divided, it is done so equally because both have equal claim. This ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah and is the relied-upon position.

Key Terms
بَيِّنَة (bayyinah): Legal evidence, typically testimony of two witnesses or one man and two women, presented to prove a claim.
تَهَاتُر (tahatur): Mutual dropping of both claims due to equal strength of evidence, resulting in both claims being invalidated.
قُرْعَة (qur'ah): Casting lots to determine the winner when evidence is equal and distinction is impossible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when two claimants each present evidence for an item in a third party's possession, what is the judgment?
A) The item is given to the one who has possession.
B) The item is divided equally between the two claimants.
C) Both claims are rejected and the item stays with the possessor.
D) Lots are cast to determine the owner.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school divides the item equally because both testimonies can be reconciled by considering different bases of ownership.

Ruling When Two Men Claim Marriage to the Same Woman with Evidence
Ruling that no judgment is given for either when two men claim marriage to the same woman with evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when two men each claim marriage to the same woman with evidence, and explain the rationale based on the indivisibility of marriage.

Core Idea
When two men each produce evidence of marriage to the same woman, neither evidence is accepted — marriage cannot be shared.

This lesson examines a foundational principle of Hanafi evidence law: the distinction between divisible and indivisible rights. When two men each claim marriage to the same woman and present evidence, the judge cannot accept either claim because a woman cannot be married to two men at once. Unlike property, which can be divided, marriage is a unitary bond that cannot be shared.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim
Two men each claim nikah with the same woman and present witnesses.
2
State the ruling
The judge does not accept either evidence (la yuqda bi waḥidatin min al-bayyinātayn).
From the matn: 'lam yuqda bi waḥidatin min al-bayyinatayn'
3
Understand the rationale
The reason is 'ta‘adhdhur al-‘amal bihimā' – it is impossible to act upon both evidences.
4
Contrast with property
In property disputes, the item can be divided between claimants; marriage is indivisible, so no division is possible.
This contrast is key to understanding the Hanafi distinction.
5
Apply the consequence
The woman remains in her original state (e.g., unmarried if she was unmarried before the claims).

قَالَ فَإِنِ ادَّعَى كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا نِكَاحَ امْرَأَةٍ وَأَقَامَا بَيْنَةً لَمْ يُقْضَ بِوَاحِدَةٍ مِنَ الْبَيِّنَتَيْنِ لِتَعَدُّرِ الْعَمَلِ بِهِمَا
He said: If each of them claims the marriage of a woman and they produce evidence, then no judgment is given by either of the two evidences because it is impossible to act upon both.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This is a ruling from the matn stating that when two men each claim to be married to the same woman and both produce evidence, the judge does not accept either evidence. The reason is that it is impossible to implement both—a woman cannot be married to two men at the same time. Unlike the case of an item, which can be divided, marriage is indivisible. Therefore, neither evidence is accepted, and the woman remains as she was. This ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah and is based on the impossibility of acting on both claims.

Key Terms
نِكَاح (nikah): Marriage contract, which is indivisible and cannot be shared between two men simultaneously.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when two men each claim marriage to the same woman and both produce evidence, what is the ruling?
A) The woman is divided between the two men.
B) Lots are cast to determine the husband.
C) Neither evidence is accepted, and the woman remains as she was.
D) The woman chooses her husband.

Key Takeaway
When two men each claim marriage to the same woman with evidence, neither evidence is accepted due to the indivisibility of marriage.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate

Disputes over Property with Multiple Claimants and Dated Evidence
Commentary on rules for multiple claimants with and without possession and dated evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply Hanafi rules for resolving property disputes among multiple claimants with dated evidence, distinguishing when dates determine priority and when they do not.

Core Idea
When claimants derive title from the same source, earlier date prevails; from different sources, they are equal.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah examines the intricate rules of judicial evidence (bayyinah) in property disputes. It addresses scenarios where multiple claimants either share a common source of title or derive ownership from different sources, and when possession influences the outcome. You will learn the principles that guide a Hanafi judge in preferring one claim over another, especially the role of dates and the concept of transfer (daf‘).

Guided Path
1
Identify the source of title for each claimant
Determine whether the claimants derive ownership from the same person (e.g., both purchased from the same seller) or from different persons (e.g., one purchased from Zaid, another inherited from his father).
The Hanafi rule changes fundamentally based on this distinction.
2
Apply the rule for same source
If all claimants derive title from the same source, the one with the earlier date of evidence is preferred because ownership can only be transferred from that source, and the earlier date shows precedence.
This is the case where dates are decisive.
3
Apply the rule for different sources
If claimants derive title from different sources (different sellers or different modes like purchase, gift, inheritance), dates become irrelevant. The property is divided equally among them regardless of dates.
Even if one claimant provides a date and another does not, the division is equal.
4
Analyze the possessor vs outsider scenario
When the outsider (non-possessor) has dated evidence and the possessor has evidence with an earlier date, the possessor wins according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. The reasoning: the possessor’s evidence implies that he derived ownership first and then transferred it to the outsider, rebutting the outsider's claim.
This is based on the concept of daf‘ (transfer).
5
Understand the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Muhammad (in one narration) disagreed: he held that both pieces of evidence are on absolute ownership, and dates are irrelevant because the cause of ownership is not specified. Thus, no preference is given to the possessor.
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of the two shaykhs.

باب ما يدعيه الرجلان. كان البائع واحدًا لأنهما اتفقا على أن الملك لا يتلقى إلا من جهته فإذا أثبت احداهما تاريخًا حتى يتبين أنه تقدمه شراء غيره ولو ادعى احداهما الشراء من رجل والآخر الهبة والقبض من غيره والثالث الميراث من أبيه والرابع الصدقة والقبض من آخر قضى بينهم أرباعًا لأنهم يتلقون الملك من بائعهم فيجعل كأنهم حضروا وأقاموا البينة على الملك المطلق.
ترجمہ: اگر دو غیر قابضوں نے بینہ قائم کیا ملک اور تاریخ پر تو سابق تاریخ والا اولی ہے کیونکہ اس نے ثابت کیا ہے کہ وہ دو مالکوں میں سے اول ہے تو ملک اسی کی طرف سے حاصل ہو سکتی ہے جلا نگہ دوسرے نے اس کی طرف سے حاصل نہیں کی۔ اگر دونوں نے دعوی کیا خرید کا ایک شخص سے۔ یعنی غیر قابض سے۔ اور دونوں نے بینہ کیا دو تاریخوں پر تو پہلی تاریخ والا اولی ہے۔ کیونکہ ہم نے بیان کیا کہ اس نے خرید ایسے وقت میں ثابت کی جس میں اس کا کوئی مزاحم نہیں۔ اور اگر ہر ایک نے بینہ قائم کیا دوسرے سے خریدنے پر اور دونوں نے تاریخ ذکر کی تو دونوں برابر ہیں۔ کیونکہ وہ اپنے اپنے بائع کے لئے ملک ثابت کر رہے ہیں تو ایسا ہو گیا کہ گویاوہ دونوں ایک ساتھ حاضر ہوئے پھر ہر ایک کو اختیار دیا جائے گا۔ جیسا کہ ہم نے سابق میں ذکر کیا۔ اور اگر ایک بینہ نے وقت بیان کیا دوسرے نے بیان نہیں کیا تو دونوں میں نصف نصف کا حکم دیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ ایک کا وقت بیان کرنا تقدم ملک پر دلالت نہیں کرتا۔ کیونکہ ممکن ہے دوسرا اس سے سابق ہو بخلاف اس کے جب بائع ایک ہو اس لئے کہ وہ دونوں اس پر متفق ہیں کہ ملک حاصل نہیں ہو سکتی ۔ مگر اسی کی جہت سے۔ پس جب ان میں سے ایک نے تاریخ ثابت کی تو اس کے لئے حکم دے دیا جائے گا۔ یہاں تک کہ یہ ظاہر ہو کہ دوسرے کی خرید اس سے پہلے ہے۔ اگر ایک نے دعوی کیا ایک شخص سے خریدنے کا اور دوسرے نے ہبہ مع القبض کا کسی اور سے اور تیسرے نے میراث کا اپنے باپ سے اور چوتھے نے صدقہ مع القبض کا کسی اور شخص سے تو حکم دیا جائے گا۔ ان میں چوتھائی چوتھائی کا کیونکہ وہ سب اپنے اپنے مملک سے تحصیل علم کے مدعی ہیں ۔ تو یوں قرار دیا جائے گا۔ کہ گویا وہ چاروں مملک خود حاضر ہوئے اور انہوں نے ملک مطلق پر بینہ قائم کیا۔
تشریح: قوله وان اقام الخارجان ... ایک مال عین کسی قابض کے قبضہ میں ہے۔ اس پر دو مدعیوں نے اپنی ملک مطلق کا دعویٰ کیا یعنی کہا کہ یہ چیز میری ہے اور خرید یا میراث وغیرہ ملک کا کوئی سبب بیان نہیں کیا۔ البتہ ملکیت کی تاریخ بیان کی اور اسی کے مطابق گواہوں نے گواہی دی۔ مثلا ایک نے رمضان ۱۳۰۵ بتلائی اور دوسرے نے محرم ۱۳۰۴ تو حکم سابق تاریخ والے کے لئے ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس کا اول مالک ہونا ثابت ہو گیا۔ پس دوسرے کو ملک اسی کی طرف سے مل سکتی ہے۔ حالانکہ اس نے یہ دعوی نہیں کیا کہ میں نے خرید یا ہبہ وغیرہ کے ذریعہ ملک اس کی طرف سے پائی ہے۔ لہذا اس کا دعویٰ خارج ہوگا۔
قوله وان اقام كل واحد منهما .... اور اگر دو مدعیوں میں سے ہر ایک نے ایک علیحدہ شخص (غیر قابض) سے خریدنے پر بینہ قائم کیا۔ مثلاً ایک نے زید سے اور دوسرے نے عمرہ سے خریدنے پر بینہ قائم کیا۔ اور دونوں نے ایک ہی تاریخ بیان کی تو دونوں برابر ہوں گے اور خریدی ہوئی چیز دونوں کے درمیان نصفا نصف ہوگی۔ کیونکہ وہ دونوں اپنے اپنے بائع کے لئے ملک ثابت کر رہے ہیں۔ تو یہ ایسا ہوگیا جیسے وہ دونوں بائع حاضر ہوں اور دعوی کریں اور دونوں ایک تاریخ کا ذکر کریں۔
قوله ولو وقت اور اگر اسی مسئلہ میں گواہوں کے ایک فریق نے تاریخ بیان کی اور دوسرے نے نہیں۔ تب بھی مبیع دونوں میں نصف نصف ہوگی۔ کیونکہ ایک فریق کا تاریخ بیان کرنا اس امر کی دلیل نہیں ہے کہ ملک اس کے لئے سابقاً ثابت تھی۔ کیونکہ ممکن ہے دوسرا اس سے سابق ہو۔ بخلاف اس کے اگر دونوں کا بائع ایک ہی شخص ہو کہ اس میں یہ احتمال نہیں۔ کیونکہ دونوں مدعی اس بات پر متفق ہیں کہ ملک کا حصول اسی بائع کی طرف سے ممکن ہے۔ پس جب ان میں سے ایک نے تاریخ بیان کی تو حکم اس کے لئے کیا جائے گا۔ تا آنکہ یہ بات ظاہر ہو کہ دوسرے کی خرید اس سے پہلے واقع ہوئی ہے۔
قوله ولوادعى احدهما الشراء ..... اور اگر دونوں میں سے ایک نے بائع سے خریدنے کا اور دوسرے نے کسی مالک سے ہبہ مع القبض کا اور تیسرے نے اپنے باپ سے میراث پانے کا اور چوتھے نے کسی شخص سے صدقہ مع القبض کا دعوی کیا تو ان چاروں میں سے ہر ایک کے لئے ایک چوتھائی کا حکم دیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ ان میں ہر ایک مدعی اپنے مملک کی طرف سے حصول ملک کا مدعی ہے تو ایسا ہو گیا جیسے گویا ان چاروں مملکوں نے خود حاضر ہو کر اپنی اپنی ملک مطلق پر بینہ قائم کیا ہے۔
قوله من باعتهم بعض نسخوں میں "من با سہم" ہے یہ دونوں بطریق تغلیب ہیں۔ کیونکہ ملکین اربعہ میں سے بائع تو صرف ایک ہے۔ اور بعض نسخوں میں "من ملقبهم" ہے۔ استدلا لا بلفظ يتلقون۔
غیر قابض نے بینہ قائم کئے ملک مورخ پر اور قبضہ والے نے تقدیر تاریخ پر بینہ قائم کئے تو قابض اولی ہے
قال فإن أقام الخارج البينة على ملك مؤرخ وصاحب اليد بينة على ملك أقدم تاريخًا كان أولى وهذا عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف وهو رواية عن محمد وعنه أنه لا يقبل بينه في اليد رجع إليه لأن البينتين قامتا على مطلق الملك ولم يتعرضا لجهة الملك فكان التقدم والتأخر سواء ولهما أن البينة مع التاريخ متضمنة معنى الدفع فإن الملك إذا ثبت لشخص في وقت فتبوته لغيره بعده لا يكون إلا بالتلقى من جهته وبينة ذي اليد على الدفع مقبولة وعلى هذا الاختلاف لو كانت الدار في أيديهما والمعنى ما بينا ولو أقام الخارج وذو اليد البينة على ملك مطلق ووقت إحداهما دون الأخرى فعلى قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد الخارج أولى وقال أبو يوسف وهو رواية عن أبي حنيفة صاحب الوقت أولى لأنه أقدم وصار كما في دعوى الشراء إذا أُرخّت إحداهما كان صاحب التاريخ أولى ولهما أن بينة ذي اليد إنما تقبل لتضمنها معنى الدفع ولا دفع ههنا حيث وقع الشك في التلقي من جهته وعلى هذا إذا كانت الدار في أيديهما ولو كانت في يد ثالث والمسألة بحالها فهما سواء عند أبي حنيفة وقال أبو يوسف الذي وقت أولى وقال محمد الذي أطلق أولى لأنه ادعى أولية الملك بدليل استحقاق الزوائد ورجوع الباعة بعضهم على البعض ولا بي يوسف أن التاريخ يوجب الملك في ذلك الوقت بيقين والإطلاق يحتمل غير الأولية والترجيح باليقين كما لو ادعها الشراء ولابي حنيفة أن التاريخ يزاحمه احتمال عدم التقدم فسقط اعتباره فصار كما إذا أقاما البينة على ملك بخلاف الشراء لأنه أمر حادث فيضاف إلى أقرب الأوقات فيترجح جانب صاحب التاريخ
ترجمہ: اگر یہ قائم کیا غیر قابض نے ملک مورخ پر اور قابض نے ایسی ملک پر جو اس کی تاریخ سے پہلے ہے۔ تو قابض اولی ہوگا ۔ یہ شیخین کے نزدیک ہے اور یہی امام محمد سے ایک روایت ہے اور ان سے روایت یہ ہے کہ قابض کا بینہ قبول نہ ہو گا۔ آپ نے اسی کی طرف رجوع کیا ہے۔ کیونکہ دونوں بینے مطلق ملک پر قائم ہوئے ہیں۔ اور سبب ملک سے کسی نے تعرض نہیں کیا۔ پس تقدم و تاخر برابر ہیں۔ شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ بینہ مع تاریخ سبب
Chapter on what the two men claim. If the seller is one, because they agreed that ownership is only derived from his side, so when one of them establishes a date until it becomes clear that his purchase preceded the other's... And if one claimed purchase from a man, another claimed gift with possession from someone else, a third claimed inheritance from his father, and a fourth claimed charity with possession from another, the judge would decree a quarter for each because they derive ownership from their sources, so it is as if they were present and established evidence of absolute ownership. 
Translation: If two non-possessors established evidence of ownership and date, the one with the earlier date is preferable because he has proven that he is the first of the two owners, so ownership can only be acquired from him, not from the other. If both claimed purchase from one person (i.e., a non-possessor) and both presented evidence with two dates, the one with the earlier date is preferable. If each established evidence of purchase from another and both mentioned a date, they are equal because they are proving ownership for their respective sellers, so it is as if both sellers were present together, then each will be given discretion. If one evidence mentioned a time and the other did not, judgment will be for half and half, because mentioning a time does not indicate precedence of ownership, as it is possible the other preceded, unlike when the seller is one, because they both agree that ownership can only be acquired from him. So when one proves a date, judgment will be given for him until it becomes clear that the other's purchase preceded his. If one claimed purchase from a person, another claimed gift with possession from someone else, a third claimed inheritance from his father, and a fourth claimed charity with possession from another person, judgment will be for a quarter each because they all claim acquisition from their respective donors, so it is as if the four donors themselves were present and established evidence of absolute ownership.
Commentary: His statement "And if the two outsiders established evidence..." There is an asset in the possession of a possessor. Two claimants claimed absolute ownership, i.e., they said this thing is mine and did not mention any cause of ownership like purchase or inheritance. However, they mentioned a date of ownership and the witnesses testified accordingly. For example, one mentioned Ramadan 1305 and the other Muharram 1304, then judgment will be for the one with the earlier date because his being the first owner is proven. So the other can only acquire ownership from him, even though he did not claim that he acquired ownership from him through purchase or gift. Therefore his claim is dismissed.
His statement "And if each of them established evidence..." If each of the two claimants established evidence of purchase from a separate person (non-possessor), e.g., one from Zaid and the other from Amr, and both mentioned the same date, then they are equal and the purchased item will be divided equally between them. If in the same issue one party of witnesses mentioned a date and the other did not, the sold item is still divided equally between them, because mentioning a date by one party does not prove that ownership was earlier for him, as the other may have preceded. Unlike if both their seller is the same person, where this possibility does not exist because both claimants agree that ownership can only be acquired from that seller. So when one mentions a date, judgment will be given for him until it becomes clear that the other's purchase occurred before his.
His statement "And if one claimed purchase..." If one of them claimed purchase from a seller, another claimed gift with possession from an owner, a third claimed inheritance from his father, and a fourth claimed charity with possession from a person, then each of the four will be decreed a quarter, because each claimant claims acquisition from his own donor, so it is as if the four donors themselves were present and established evidence of their absolute ownership.
His statement "from their sellers" in some manuscripts is "from their..." both are by way of predominance, because among the four owners only one is a seller. And in some manuscripts it is "from their sources" as indicated by the word "yatalaqqawna" (they derive).
The non-possessor established evidence of dated ownership and the possessor established evidence of a more ancient date, then the possessor is preferable.
He said: If the outsider establishes evidence of dated ownership and the possessor establishes evidence of ownership with an earlier date, then the possessor is preferable, according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and it is a narration from Muhammad. And from him it is narrated that the evidence of the possessor is not accepted; he reverted to this, because the two evidences are based on absolute ownership and did not address the cause of ownership, so precedence and delay are equal. Their argument: evidence with a date implies the meaning of transfer (daf'), because if ownership is proven for a person at a time, its proof for another after that can only be by derivation from him, and the evidence of the possessor regarding transfer is accepted. According to this difference, if the house is in the hands of both, the meaning is as we explained. And if the outsider and the possessor establish evidence of absolute ownership and one of them specifies a time while the other does not, then according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad the outsider is preferable. Abu Yusuf said, and it is a narration from Abu Hanifa, that the one with the time is preferable because his time is earlier, and it becomes like the claim of purchase when one of the two evidences is dated, the one with the date is preferable. Their argument: The evidence of the possessor is only accepted because it implies the meaning of transfer, but there is no transfer here where there is doubt about derivation from his side. According to this, if the house is in the hands of both, or if it is in the hand of a third party and the issue remains the same, they are equal according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf said the one who specified a time is preferable. Muhammad said the one who did not specify is preferable because he claimed priority of ownership by evidence of entitlement to increments and recourse of sellers among themselves. Abu Yusuf: The date necessitates ownership at that time with certainty, and absolute evidence admits other than priority, and preference is given by certainty, as in the claim of purchase. Abu Hanifa: The date is countered by the possibility of non-priority, so its consideration falls, making it as if they both established evidence of ownership, unlike purchase because it is a temporary matter attributed to the nearest time, so the side of the one with the date is preferred.
Translation: If the non-possessor established evidence of dated ownership and the possessor established evidence of ownership earlier than that date, then the possessor is preferable. This is according to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and it is a narration from Muhammad. And from him it is narrated that the evidence of the possessor will not be accepted; he reverted to this, because both evidences are established on absolute ownership and did not address the cause of ownership, so precedence and delay are equal. The argument of the two shaykhs: Evidence with a date implies the meaning of transfer.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya discusses the rules of evidence in property disputes when multiple claimants are involved. It begins by explaining the case where two non-possessors each claim ownership and present dated evidence. The key principle is that if the claimants derive their title from the same source (e.g., both purchased from the same seller), the earlier date prevails because ownership can only be transferred from that source. However, if they derive title from different sources (e.g., one purchased from Zaid, another from Amr), they are treated as equal, and the property is divided equally even if one has a date and the other does not. The reason is that the date from one source does not prove precedence over the other's source. The passage then moves to a scenario where claimants have different modes of acquisition (purchase, gift, inheritance, charity) from different donors; here, the property is divided equally because each claimant's title comes from a different donor, and it is as if the donors themselves are present and claim absolute ownership. Finally, the text presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: when the outsider (non-possessor) brings dated evidence and the possessor brings evidence of an earlier date, the possessor is preferred according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (and one narration from Muhammad), but another narration from Muhammad says the possessor's evidence is not accepted because both are absolute claims. The reasoning involves the concept of 'daf'' (transfer) – the possessor's evidence implies that he derived ownership from the outsider's earlier owner. The different positions of the imams are explained with rational arguments (talil). The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of the two shaykhs preferring the possessor with the earlier date.

Key Terms
بينة (bayyinah): Legal evidence, usually testimony of witnesses.
تاريخ (ta'rikh): Date or time specified in the evidence to indicate when ownership was established.
ملك (milk): Ownership or property right.
قابض (qabid): Possessor; the person who has physical control over the property.
خارج (kharij): Outsider; the claimant who does not have possession.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, if a non-possessor (outsider) brings evidence of ownership with a date of 2020 and the possessor brings evidence of ownership with a date of 2010, what is the ruling?
A) The property is divided equally because both have evidence of ownership.
B) The possessor is preferable because his date is earlier, implying he transferred ownership to the outsider.
C) The outsider is preferable because he has a specific date.
D) The case is dismissed because the dates are contradictory.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the priority of dated evidence depends on whether claimants share a common source of title; if they do, earlier date wins; if not, dates are irrelevant.

Qada — Judiciary

Rules of Bayyinah in Ownership Disputes: Possessor's Preference and Effect of Dates
Rules of evidence in ownership claims with possession and dates

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that the possessor's bayyinah is preferred when both claimants present equal evidence of absolute ownership without dates, and distinguish the effect of dates in absolute ownership versus purchase claims.

Core Idea
When evidence is equal, possession (yad) tips the scale; dates matter only for recent events like purchase.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah examines the rules of evidence when two claimants dispute ownership. The key principle: if both present equal bayyinah on absolute ownership without mentioning dates, the possessor's evidence is preferred. But when dates are introduced, a nuanced intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf emerges. Understanding these rules is crucial for qada (judicial procedure).

Guided Path
1
Identify the baseline scenario
Both claimants present bayyinah on absolute ownership (milk mutlaq) without mentioning any date. One is the possessor (qabid), the other is the external claimant (ghayr qabid).
This is the simplest case; the ruling is agreed upon (bil-ittifaq).
2
Apply the agreed Hanafi ruling
The possessor's bayyinah is preferred because his possession (yad) gives additional weight. The text states: 'when they establish bayyinah on absolute ownership without mentioning a date, then by agreement the possessor's bayyinah is accepted.'
The reason: the possessor's bayyinah inherently implies repelling (daf') the external claim.
3
Recognize the ikhtilaf when one bayyinah includes a date
If one claimant's bayyinah mentions a date and the other's does not, there is disagreement: Abu Hanifa (known view) disregards the date; Abu Yusuf and a narration from Abu Hanifa prefer the dated evidence; Muhammad prefers the absolute claim without date.
The text presents the proofs for each position.
4
Analyze the reasoning behind each position
Abu Hanifa: the date is disregarded because of the possibility that the non-dated claim may be earlier (no certainty of priority). Abu Yusuf: the date establishes ownership with certainty from that time, and certainty outweighs probability. Muhammad: absolute ownership is stronger (aqwa) as it entitles the owner to all proceeds.
The distinction from purchase (shira') is key: purchase is a recent event, so date is decisive.
5
Consider the nataj (birth) case
When both claimants present bayyinah on the birth of an animal (nataj), the possessor is preferred because the evidence is on something the hand does not indicate, so they become equal, and the hand gives weight. This is the correct position, contrary to Isa ibn Aban who says both bayyinahs cancel.
Practical consequence: in the Hanafi view, the possessor does not need to swear an oath.

کا مورخ بینہ معنی دفع خارج کو متضمن ہے۔ کیونکہ جب ایک وقت میں کسی کے لئے ملک ثابت ہو تو اس وقت کے بعد دوسرے کے لئے مالک کا ثبوت اس کی جانب سے حاصل کرنے کے ساتھ ہو سکتا ہے۔ اور دفع خصومت پر قابض کا بینہ مقبول ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا قابض کا بینہ مقدم ہوگا۔ اسی طرح اگر مکان ان دونوں کے قبضہ میں ہو تو اس میں بھی اختلاف ہے اور وجہ وہی ہے جو پہلے مذکور ہوئی کہ ملک سابق کے بعد دوسرے کو ملکیت اسی کی طرف سے حاصل ہو سکتی ہے۔

قوله الو اقام الخارج و ذوالید.... ایک مدعی غیر قابض نے اور دوسرے مدعی قابض نے اپنی اپنی ملک مطلق پر بینہ قائم کیا اور ایک مدعی کے گواہوں نے تاریخ بیان کی اور دوسرے کے گواہوں نے تاریخ بیان نہیں کی تو طرفین کے نزدیک غیر قابض اولی ہو گا۔ یعنی حکم اس کے لئے ہو گا۔ امام ابو حنیفہ سے دوسری روایت ( اور وہی امام ابو یوسف کا قول ہے ) یہ ہے کہ جس کی تاریخ سابق ہے وہی اولی ہے۔ کیونکہ وہ دوسرے سے مقدم ہے۔ پھر کتاب میں وقت احدهما “ کی قید اس لئے ہے کہ قابض و غیر قابض اگر ملک مطلق پر بینہ بلا ذکر تاریخ قائم کریں تو ہمارے یہاں بالاتفاق قابض کا بینہ مقبول ہوگا۔ فالاختلاف انما هو عند ذكر التاريخ

قوله ولهما ان بينقذى اليد .... طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ قابض کا بینہ صرف اس لئے مقبول ہوتا ہے کہ وہ متضمن دفعیہ ہوتا ہے۔ یعنی اس سے غیر قابض کا دعوی دفع ہو جاتا ہے اور یہاں کوئی دفعیہ نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے کہ جس کی تاریخ ملک مقدم ہے۔ اس کی جانب سے غیر قابض کو حصول ملک میں شک ہے۔ کہ ہو سکتا ہے۔ اس نے قابض سے ملک حاصل کی ہو۔ اسی طرح اور وہ مکان ان دونوں کے قبضہ میں ہو تب بھی یہی اختلاف ہے۔ قوله ولو كانت فى يد ثالث... اور اگر مکان کسی تیسرے کے قبضہ میں ہو اور باقی مسئلہ بحالہ ہو ( یعنی ملک مطلق کے دعوئی میں ایک غیر قابض کا بینہ مؤرخ ہو دوسرے کا مؤرخ نہ ہو ۔ تب بھی امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک دونوں مدعی برابر ہیں۔ ائمہ ثلاثہ کا قول بھی یہی ہے۔ امام ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں۔ کہ تاریخ والا بینہ اولی ہوگا۔ اور امام محمد کے نزدیک جس نے مطلق چھوڑا ہے وہ اولی ہو گا۔ اس لئے کہ جس نے تاریخ بیان نہیں کی وہ اولیت ملک کا مدعی ہے۔ بدلیل آنکہ جو شخص ملک مطلق کا مدعی ہو تو اس مال سے جو زوائد ( متصله و منفصلہ جیسے اولاد و کساب) حاصل ہوں اُن کا مستحق وہی ہوتا ہے۔ نیز اگر یہ چیز کسی نے اپنا استحقاق ثابت کر کے لے لی تو پچھلی بیع کرنے والے لوگ اپنے اپنے بائع سے برابر ثمن پھیرتے جائیں گے۔ معلوم ہوا کہ ملک مطلق اقویٰ ہے۔ امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب تاریخ مذکور ہو تو ملک بالیقین اسی وقت سے ثابت ہو جاتی ہے۔ اور ملک مطلق کے دعوئی میں یہ احتمال ہے کہ وہ اول نہ ہو۔ پس یقین کو احتمال پر ترجیح ہوگی جیسے اگر دو مدعیوں میں سے ہر ایک نے خرید کا دعوی کر کے اپنی اپنی گواہی میں تاریخ بیان کی تو جس کی تاریخ مقدم ہو وہ اولی ہوتا ہے۔

قوله ولابي حنيفة ان التاريخ امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہاں تاریخ کی مزاحمت میں یہ احتمال قائم ہے کہ شاید یہ مقدم نہ ہو۔ یعنی تاریخ کے وقت سے ملکیت اگر چہ یقینی ہے لیکن ملک مطلق کے مدعی سے اس کا مقدم ہونا یقینی نہیں۔ لہذا تاریخ کا اعتبار ساقط ہو گیا۔ پس ایسا ہو گیا کہ گویا دونوں نے بلا تاریخ ملک مطلق پر بینے قائم کئے۔ اور اس میں دونوں کے مساوی ہونے کا حکم ہوتا ہے تو یہاں بھی یہی ہوگا۔ قوله بخلاف الشراء ... امام ابو یوسف کے قول كما لو ادَّعيا الشراء“ کا جواب ہے کہ بخلاف دعوی شراء کے یعنی جب ایک نے مطلق مع تاریخ کا اور دوسرے نے خرید بلا تاریخ کا دعوی کیا تو یہاں تاریخ مقدم ہے۔ کیونکہ خرید تو ایک فعل جدید واقع ہوتا ہے تو بدون تاریخ کے وہ سب سے قریب وقت کی جانب منسوب ہو گا۔ پس تاریخ والے کو اس پر ترجیح ہوگی۔ مثلاً ایک شخص نے ۱۲۸۰ھ میں اپنے باپ سے ایک گھوڑا میراث پایا جس کو کسی نے چرا کر ۱۲۸۰ھ میں زید کے ہاتھ فروخت کر دیا۔ تو یہاں خرید اصل مالک کی ملکیت کے بعد واقع ہوئی۔ اب اگر اصل مالک یہ دعوے کرے کہ میں نے اس کو ۱۲۸۰ھ میں میراث پایا ہے۔ اور زید بلا تاریخ یہ کہے کہ میں نے خریدا ہے تو حکم تاریخ والے کے لئے ہوگا۔ کیونکہ بیع تو اس کے ایک روز بعد بھی ہو سکتی ہے۔

فائدہ جب دو آدمی عین شئی کا دعوی کریں تو یہ تین حال سے خالی نہیں۔ دعویٰ ملک مطلق کا ہوگا یا شرا کا یا ارث کا۔ ان میں سے ہر ایک کی پھر تین صورتیں ہیں۔ مال عین ان میں سے کسی ایک کے قبضہ میں ہوگا۔ یا دونوں کے یا شخص ثالث کے۔ ان میں سے ہر ایک کی پھر چار صورتیں ہیں۔ دونوں نے کوئی تاریخ بیان نہیں کی ہوگی۔ یا کوئی ایک ہی تاریخ بیان کی ہوگی۔ یا ایک تاریخ مقدم اور دوسرے کی مؤخر ہوگی۔ یا ان میں سے صرف ایک نے تاریخ بیان کی ہوگی دوسرے نے نہیں۔ پس یہ ۳۲ صورتیں ہیں۔ وقد عرف ذلك في موضعه (كفايه) قابض اور غیر قابض دونوں نے بینہ قائم کئے پیدائش پر تو قابض اولی ہے

قَالَ وَإِنْ أَقَامَ الْخَارِجُ وَصَاحِبُ الْيَدِ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا بَيْنَةً عَلَى النِّتَاجِ فَصَاحِبُ الْيَدِ أَوْلَى لِأَنَّ الْبَيِّنَةَ قَامَتْ عَلى مَا لَاتَدُلُّ عَلَيْهِ الْيَدُ فَاسْتَوَيَا وَتَرَبَّحَتْ بَيْنَةُ ذِي الْيَدِ بِالْيَدِ فَيُقْضَى لَهُ وَهَذَا هُوَ الصَّحِيحُ خِلَافًا لِمَا يَقُولُهُ عِيسَى بْنُ أَيَّانٌ أَنَّهُ تَتَهَاتَرَ الْبَيِّنَتَانِ وَيُتْرَكُ فِي يَدِهِ لَا عَلَى طَرِيقِ الْقَضَاءِ ترجمہ اگر بینہ قائم کیا قابض و غیر قابض میں سے ہر ایک نے پیدائش پر تو قابض اولیٰ ہے کیونکہ بینہ اس پر قائم ہوا ہے۔ جس پر قبضہ دلالت نہیں کرتا۔ پس دونوں برابر ہو گئے اور قابض کا بینہ قبضہ کی وجہ سے راجح ہوا تو اس کے لئے حکم کیا جائے گا۔ یہی صحیح ہے۔ برخلاف اس کے جو عیسی بن ابان کہتے ہیں کہ دونوں بینے ساقط ہوں گے۔ اور چیز قابض کے قبضہ میں غیر قضا کے طور پر چھوڑ دی جائے گی۔ تشریح... قوله وان اقام الخارج شخص خارج اور قابض دونوں نے ملک کے ایسے سب پر بینہ قائم کیا۔ جو مکرر واقع نہیں ہوتا۔ ایک ہی بار ہوتا و ثمرة الخلاف انما تظهر في حق تحليف ذي اليد و عدمه فعنده يحلف ذواليد للخارج و عندنا لا يحلف
Chapter: What Two Men Claim. ... (The Urdu commentary explains that the possessor's evidence is accepted because it implies repelling the claim. When both claimants present evidence of absolute ownership without dates, the possessor is preferred. If one mentions a date, there is disagreement: Abu Yusuf and a narration from Abu Hanifa say the one with the earlier date is preferred; Abu Hanifa's other view says the date is disregarded due to possibility of non-priority. Similar disagreements when both possess or third party possesses. At the end: 'And if the external and the possessor each establish evidence on the birth (of an animal), then the possessor is preferred because the evidence was on something that the hand does not indicate, so they become equal, and the evidence of the possessor gains weight by the hand, so judgment is given to him. This is the correct position, contrary to what Isa ibn Aban says that both evidences are cancelled and it is left in the hand, not by way of judgment.')
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah is a commentary on the chapter 'Bab ma yadda'ihi al-rajulan' from al-Hidayah, discussing rules of evidence (bayyinah) when two claimants dispute ownership. The text begins by explaining the principle that the possessor's bayyinah is accepted because it inherently repels the external claim. The key ruling: when both the external claimant (kharj) and the possessor (sahib al-yad) present bayyinah on absolute ownership (milk mutlaq) without mentioning a date, the possessor's bayyinah is preferred by virtue of possession. This is the agreed Hanafi position (bil-ittifaq).

When one bayyinah includes a date (tarikh) and the other does not, the text presents a known intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Imam Abu Yusuf and a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa hold that the one with the earlier date is preferred because the date establishes ownership with certainty from that time. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that the claimant who asserted absolute ownership without a date is preferred because absolute ownership is stronger (aqwa) as it entitles the owner to all proceeds (zawa'id). However, the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) according to the text is that of Abu Hanifa's other view: the date becomes irrelevant because there is a possibility that the dated ownership is not earlier, so both are treated as equal, and the rule for absolute ownership without dates applies (possessor is preferred if he is the one with the hand, otherwise the external is preferred when both are non-possessors or third party holds).

Further sub-scenarios: if both claimants are in possession, the same ikhtilaf applies. If a third party possesses, Abu Hanifa says both claimants are equal; Abu Yusuf prefers the one with the date; Muhammad prefers the one with absolute claim. The text also notes a specific ruling about 'nataj' (birth/offspring of an animal): when both claimants present bayyinah on the birth (i.e., ownership of the offspring), the possessor is preferred because the evidence does not indicate the hand, so they become equal, and the hand gives weight. This is the correct Hanafi position, contrary to Isa ibn Aban who says both bayyinahs cancel out and the item remains with the possessor without formal judgment. The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of this difference is whether the possessor must swear an oath (tahlif) to the external claimant: according to Isa, he does swear; according to the Hanafis, he does not.

The commentator also provides a useful classification: ownership claims can be of absolute milk, purchase (shira'), or inheritance (irth). Each has three situations regarding possession, and each has four situations regarding mention of dates, yielding 32 total scenarios.

Key Terms
بينة (bayyinah): Evidence, usually two male witnesses, presented in court to prove a claim.
قابض (qabid): The person in physical possession of the disputed property.
غير قابض (ghayr qabid): The external claimant who does not have possession.
ملک مطلق (milk mutlaq): Absolute ownership without specifying how it was acquired (e.g., not purchase or inheritance).
تاریخ (tarikh): Date mentioned by witnesses to specify when the claimant acquired ownership.
دفع (daf'): Repelling the opponent's claim; the possessor's bayyinah inherently includes a defensive element.
نتاج (nataj): Birth of an animal; ownership of the offspring is derived from ownership of the mother.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If both a possessor and an external claimant establish bayyinah on absolute ownership (milk mutlaq) without mentioning any date, whose evidence is preferred according to the reliable Hanafi position?
A) The external claimant's, because he is the plaintiff.
B) The possessor's, because the hand strengthens his evidence.
C) Neither; both bayyinahs cancel out.
D) It depends on the judge's discretion.

Key Takeaway
The possessor's bayyinah is preferred when evidence is equal on absolute ownership without dates; dates are disregarded for absolute ownership but decisive for purchase.
