Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a ruling from Al-Hidayah regarding the priority of evidence when multiple parties claim ownership of a property. The opening line identifies the chapter on what two men claim (باب ما يدعيه الرجلان). The commentator explains the vocabulary, then translates the ruling. The core principle is that evidence of birth (نتاج) — meaning that the property was born from an animal or slave owned by the claimant — is considered stronger than evidence of absolute ownership (ملک مطلق). This is because birth evidence is like a definitive text (نص) that leaves no room for ijtihad, whereas absolute ownership claims are based on ijtihad. Therefore, if a person was defeated in a case of absolute ownership, they can later bring evidence of birth and overturn the previous judgment. The commentary then extends this analogy to non-repetitive causes of ownership like milking, cheese-making, etc., versus repetitive causes like building, planting, and cultivating. If there is doubt, experts are consulted; if even experts cannot decide, the original principle (judgment for the non-possessor) prevails. The passage also covers the scenario where a non-possessor claims absolute ownership and the possessor claims purchase from that non-possessor — here the possessor is preferred because the two claims are not contradictory; the possessor is essentially acknowledging the other's ownership and then claiming a transfer from him.

Key Terms
سبب مكرر (sabab mukarrar): A repetitive cause of ownership, like building, planting, weaving, which can be done many times.
الأصل (al-asl): The original principle that judgment is given based on the non-possessor's evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling when there is ambiguity about whether a cause is repetitive or non-repetitive, and experts cannot resolve it?
A) Judgment for the possessor
B) Judgment for the non-possessor
C) The property is divided
D) The case is dismissed

Key Takeaway
Repetitive causes of ownership do not override the original principle; when in doubt, judgment goes to the non-possessor.

Qada — Judiciary

Overturning Prior Judgment with Birth Evidence
Procedural rule: birth evidence can overturn prior judgments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that a prior judgment based on absolute ownership can be overturned by later birth evidence, and also that a third claimant can overturn a birth-based judgment unless the possessor re-presents evidence.

Core Idea
Birth evidence can overturn a prior judgment; a third claimant can also overturn unless the first re-proves birth.

The strength of birth evidence is such that it can overturn a prior judgment based on absolute ownership. Even a third claimant (not party to the first case) can bring birth evidence and overturn a judgment for the possessor, unless the possessor re-presents his birth evidence. This lesson examines these procedural aspects.

Guided Path
1
Case 1: Overturning an absolute ownership judgment
A person loses a case based on absolute ownership. Later, he finds evidence of birth. His birth evidence is accepted and overturns the prior judgment.
This is because birth evidence is like نص that overrides previous ijtihad.
2
Case 2: Third claimant after birth-based judgment
If judgment was given for the possessor based on birth, a third claimant can bring birth evidence and overturn, unless the possessor re-proves his birth evidence.
The third claimant was not a party to the first judgment.

کرنا، پھر اگر مشتبہ ہو تو ہوشیار لوگوں کی طرف رجوع کیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ وہ اس کے زیادہ جان کار ہیں۔ اگر اُن پر بھی مشتبہ رہے تو غیر قابض کے لئے حکم ہوگا۔ اس لئے کہ اس کے بینہ سے حکم ہونا ہی اصل ہے۔ اور اس سے عدول خبر نتاج کی وجہ سے تھا۔ اور جب یہ معلوم نہیں ہوا تو اصل کی طرف رجوع کیا جائے گا۔ اگر ہیتہ قائم کیا غیر قابض نے ملک مطلق پر اور قابض نے اس سے خریدنے پر تو قابض اولی ہو گا۔ اس لئے کہ اول نے اگر چہ ملک کی اولیت ثابت کی ہے مگر قابض نے اس سے حصول ثابت کیا ہے۔ اور اس میں کوئی منافات نہیں۔ تو ایسا ہو گیا جیسے قابض نے غیر کے لئے ملک کا اقرار کیا پھر اس سے خرید لینے کا دعویٰ کیا۔ تشریح ... قوله ولو تلقى كل واحد .. اگر قابض میں سے ہر ایک نے کسی شخص کی طرف سے حصول ملک کا دعوی کر کے اس امر پر بینے قائم کئے کہ یہ چیز اس کے پاس اس کی مملوکہ چیز سے پیدا ہوئی ہے۔ مثلاً زید کے قبضہ میں ایک غلام ہے۔ اس پر بکر نے دعوے کیا کہ میں نے یہ غلام خالد سے خریدا ہے جو خالد کی ملک میں اس کی مملوکہ باندی سے پیدا ہوا تھا۔ اور قابض (زید) نے ہینہ قائم کیا۔ کہ میں نے یہ غلام عمر و سے خریدا ہے جو اس کی ملک میں اس کی مملوکہ باندی سے پیدا ہوا تھا۔ تو قابض کو تربیج ہو کر حکم اس کے لئے ہوگا۔

قوله ولو قضى بالنتاج .. اگر قابض کے لئے بذریعہ نتاج حکم دے دیا گیا پھر تیسرے مدعی نے بہینہ قائم کیا کہ یہ میری مملوکہ سے میری ملک میں پیدا ہوا ہے۔ تو تیسرے کے لئے حکم دے دیا جائے گا۔ مگر یہ کہ قابض اپنابینہ دوبارہ پیش کرے۔ اس لئے کہ قابض کے واسطے حکم ہو جانے میں تیسرا مدعی تحت القضا داخل نہیں ہوا یعنی اس پر یہ حکم نہیں ہوا کہ اس کا دعوئی خارج ہے۔ اسی طرح جو شخص ملک مطلق کے دعوئی میں مقتضی علیہ ہو جائے یعنی وہ خارج کر دیا جائے اور مدعی کے لئے حکم ہو جائے پھر وہ نتاج پر بینہ لائے تو قبول ہوگا۔ اور اس کے ذریعہ سے حکم اول تو ڑ دیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ نتاج کا حکم بمنزلہ نص ہے اور اول بمنزلہ اجتہاد اور مجتہد کو جب اس کے اجتہاد کے خلاف نص مل جائے تو حکم اول ٹوٹ کر نص کے موافق حکم ہوتا ہے تو ایسے ہی یہاں ہوگا۔

فائدہ ... مقضی علیہ بملک مطلق کی مثال یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص کے قبضہ میں ایک چوپایہ ہے اس پر زید نے ملک مطلق کا دعوی کر کے ہینہ قائم کیا جس کے نتیجہ میں چوپایہ زید کو دلا دیا گیا۔ پس وہ شخص مقضی علیہ اور زید مقضی لہ ہے۔ اب اگر قابض نتاج پر ہینہ قائم کرنے تو مقبول ہو گا اور زید کے لئے جو حکم ہو تھا وہ ٹوٹ جائے گا۔ قوله وان اقام الخارج مشخص خارج ( غیر قابض) نے ملک مطلق پر ہینہ قائم کیا اور قابض نے اس بات پر کہ میں نے شخص خارج سے خریدا ہے تو قابض کا بینہ معتبر ہوگا۔ کیونکہ مشخص خارج اولیت ملک کو ثابت کر رہا ہے۔ اور قابض اس سے ملک حاصل کر دونوں میں کوئی منافات نہیں تو ایسا ہو گیا جیسے قابض نے پہلے غیر کے لئے ملکیت کا اقرار کیا۔ پھر اس سے خرید لینے کا دعویٰ کیا۔
Translation: If each of them claims acquisition of ownership from a person and establishes evidence that it was born in his possession, then it is like establishing evidence of birth in his own possession. If one establishes evidence of ownership and the other of birth, the one with birth evidence is preferred, regardless, because his evidence is prior in establishing ownership, so ownership is not established for the other except through his direction. Similarly, if the claim is between two non-possessors, the evidence of birth is preferred. If judgment has been given [to the possessor], and the possessor presents evidence again, because the third claimant was not a party to the judgment. Similarly, the one against whom a judgment of absolute ownership has been passed, if he brings evidence of birth, it will be accepted and the first judgment will be overtured, because this is like a definitive text (nas) and the first is like ijtihad. Similarly, for items that are not manufactured repeatedly, like cotton cloth, and every cause of ownership that is not repetitive, because it is in the sense of birth (natal), like milking, cheese-making, felting, shearing wool, trimming goat hair. And if it is repetitive, then judgment will be for the non-possessor, like absolute ownership, e.g., wool cloth, building construction, planting, cultivating wheat and grains. Then if there is ambiguity, experts are consulted. If they remain ambiguous, judgment is for the non-possessor, because the original principle is that judgment is given on his evidence, and deviation from that was due to the nature of birth; when that is unknown, we revert to the original. If a non-possessor establishes evidence of absolute ownership and the possessor establishes evidence of purchase from him, the possessor is preferred, because although the first established priority of ownership, the possessor established acquisition from him, and there is no contradiction. So it is as if the possessor acknowledged ownership for the other and then claimed purchase from him. Explanation: His statement 'And if each one receives...': If each of the possessors claims acquisition of ownership from a person and establishes evidence that this thing was born from his owned property in his possession, e.g., Zayd has a slave in his possession, and Bakr claims, 'I bought this slave from Khalid, and he was born from a slave-girl owned by Khalid,' and the possessor (Zayd) establishes evidence that he bought the slave from 'Amr, who owned the slave-girl, then the possessor is given preference and judgment is for him. His statement 'And if judgment was given by birth...': If judgment was given for the possessor by means of birth, then a third claimant brings evidence that it was born from his own owned property in his ownership, then judgment will be given for the third, unless the possessor presents his evidence again. Because the third claimant was not under the judgment that his claim is rejected. Similarly, a person who was made the defendant in a case of absolute ownership (i.e., he was dispossessed) and judgment was given for the claimant, then if he brings evidence of birth, it will be accepted and the first judgment will be overtured, because the ruling of birth is like a text (nas) and the first is like ijtihad. When a mujtahid finds a text contrary to his ijtihad, the first judgment is broken and a judgment in accordance with the text is given. So here too. Benefit: Example of a defendant in absolute ownership: A person has an animal in his possession, and Zayd claims absolute ownership and establishes evidence, resulting in the animal being given to Zayd. So that person is the defendant and Zayd is the claimant. Now if the possessor establishes evidence of birth, it will be accepted and the judgment for Zayd will be overtured. His statement 'And if the outsider establishes...': If the outsider (non-possessor) establishes evidence of absolute ownership and the possessor establishes that he bought from that outsider, then the possessor's evidence is considered, because the outsider is proving priority of ownership, and the possessor is proving acquisition from him, and there is no contradiction. So it is as if the possessor first acknowledged ownership for the outsider and then claimed purchase from him.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a ruling from Al-Hidayah regarding the priority of evidence when multiple parties claim ownership of a property. The opening line identifies the chapter on what two men claim (باب ما يدعيه الرجلان). The commentator explains the vocabulary, then translates the ruling. The core principle is that evidence of birth (نتاج) — meaning that the property was born from an animal or slave owned by the claimant — is considered stronger than evidence of absolute ownership (ملک مطلق). This is because birth evidence is like a definitive text (نص) that leaves no room for ijtihad, whereas absolute ownership claims are based on ijtihad. Therefore, if a person was defeated in a case of absolute ownership, they can later bring evidence of birth and overturn the previous judgment. The commentary then extends this analogy to non-repetitive causes of ownership like milking, cheese-making, etc., versus repetitive causes like building, planting, and cultivating. If there is doubt, experts are consulted; if even experts cannot decide, the original principle (judgment for the non-possessor) prevails. The passage also covers the scenario where a non-possessor claims absolute ownership and the possessor claims purchase from that non-possessor — here the possessor is preferred because the two claims are not contradictory; the possessor is essentially acknowledging the other's ownership and then claiming a transfer from him.

Key Terms
مقضی علیہ (maqdi alayh): The person against whom a judgment is given (defendant).
تحت القضا (taht al-qada): Under the judgment; bound by the court's decision.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If judgment was given for a possessor based on birth evidence, and then a third claimant brings birth evidence, what condition must be met for the possessor to retain the property?
A) The third claimant must also prove absolute ownership
B) The possessor must re-present his birth evidence
C) The third claimant must accept the first judgment
D) The case is automatically dismissed

Key Takeaway
Birth evidence can overturn prior judgments; a third claimant can overturn a birth-based judgment unless the first re-proves his birth evidence.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
6 min
Purchase from Non-Possessor: Possessor Preferred
Rule: Possessor's evidence of purchase from non-possessor takes precedence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that when a non-possessor claims absolute ownership and the possessor claims purchase from that non-possessor, the possessor's evidence is preferred because there is no contradiction.

Core Idea
Possessor claiming purchase from the non-possessor is preferred because the two claims are not contradictory.

A special scenario: a non-possessor (خارج) brings evidence of absolute ownership, and the possessor brings evidence that he bought the property from that same non-possessor. The Hanafi rule: the possessor's evidence is accepted. Why? Because the non-possessor's claim of ownership does not contradict the possessor's claim of purchase from him; in fact, the possessor's evidence implicitly acknowledges the non-possessor's prior ownership. So the possessor is like a person who first acknowledged the other's ownership and then claimed a purchase from him.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and claims
The non-possessor (outsider) claims absolute ownership. The possessor claims that he bought the property from that non-possessor.
Both have evidence.
2
Analyze the relationship between claims
The possessor's claim does not deny the non-possessor's ownership; it actually affirms it and then adds a subsequent transfer.
No contradiction.
3
Apply the ruling
The possessor's evidence is preferred because it acknowledges the non-possessor's prior ownership and then proves a transfer. The judge rules for the possessor.
The analogy: it is as if the possessor first admitted the non-possessor's ownership and then claimed purchase.

فائدہ ... مقضی علیہ بملک مطلق کی مثال یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص کے قبضہ میں ایک چوپایہ ہے اس پر زید نے ملک مطلق کا دعوی کر کے ہینہ قائم کیا جس کے نتیجہ میں چوپایہ زید کو دلا دیا گیا۔ پس وہ شخص مقضی علیہ اور زید مقضی لہ ہے۔ اب اگر قابض نتاج پر ہینہ قائم کرنے تو مقبول ہو گا اور زید کے لئے جو حکم ہو تھا وہ ٹوٹ جائے گا۔ قوله وان اقام الخارج مشخص خارج ( غیر قابض) نے ملک مطلق پر ہینہ قائم کیا اور قابض نے اس بات پر کہ میں نے شخص خارج سے خریدا ہے تو قابض کا بینہ معتبر ہوگا۔ کیونکہ مشخص خارج اولیت ملک کو ثابت کر رہا ہے۔ اور قابض اس سے ملک حاصل کر دونوں میں کوئی منافات نہیں تو ایسا ہو گیا جیسے قابض نے پہلے غیر کے لئے ملکیت کا اقرار کیا۔ پھر اس سے خرید لینے کا دعویٰ کیا۔
Translation: If each of them claims acquisition of ownership from a person and establishes evidence that it was born in his possession, then it is like establishing evidence of birth in his own possession. If one establishes evidence of ownership and the other of birth, the one with birth evidence is preferred, regardless, because his evidence is prior in establishing ownership, so ownership is not established for the other except through his direction. Similarly, if the claim is between two non-possessors, the evidence of birth is preferred. If judgment has been given [to the possessor], and the possessor presents evidence again, because the third claimant was not a party to the judgment. Similarly, the one against whom a judgment of absolute ownership has been passed, if he brings evidence of birth, it will be accepted and the first judgment will be overtured, because this is like a definitive text (nas) and the first is like ijtihad. Similarly, for items that are not manufactured repeatedly, like cotton cloth, and every cause of ownership that is not repetitive, because it is in the sense of birth (natal), like milking, cheese-making, felting, shearing wool, trimming goat hair. And if it is repetitive, then judgment will be for the non-possessor, like absolute ownership, e.g., wool cloth, building construction, planting, cultivating wheat and grains. Then if there is ambiguity, experts are consulted. If they remain ambiguous, judgment is for the non-possessor, because the original principle is that judgment is given on his evidence, and deviation from that was due to the nature of birth; when that is unknown, we revert to the original. If a non-possessor establishes evidence of absolute ownership and the possessor establishes evidence of purchase from him, the possessor is preferred, because although the first established priority of ownership, the possessor established acquisition from him, and there is no contradiction. So it is as if the possessor acknowledged ownership for the other and then claimed purchase from him. Explanation: His statement 'And if each one receives...': If each of the possessors claims acquisition of ownership from a person and establishes evidence that this thing was born from his owned property in his possession, e.g., Zayd has a slave in his possession, and Bakr claims, 'I bought this slave from Khalid, and he was born from a slave-girl owned by Khalid,' and the possessor (Zayd) establishes evidence that he bought the slave from 'Amr, who owned the slave-girl, then the possessor is given preference and judgment is for him. His statement 'And if judgment was given by birth...': If judgment was given for the possessor by means of birth, then a third claimant brings evidence that it was born from his own owned property in his ownership, then judgment will be given for the third, unless the possessor presents his evidence again. Because the third claimant was not under the judgment that his claim is rejected. Similarly, a person who was made the defendant in a case of absolute ownership (i.e., he was dispossessed) and judgment was given for the claimant, then if he brings evidence of birth, it will be accepted and the first judgment will be overtured, because the ruling of birth is like a text (nas) and the first is like ijtihad. When a mujtahid finds a text contrary to his ijtihad, the first judgment is broken and a judgment in accordance with the text is given. So here too. Benefit: Example of a defendant in absolute ownership: A person has an animal in his possession, and Zayd claims absolute ownership and establishes evidence, resulting in the animal being given to Zayd. So that person is the defendant and Zayd is the claimant. Now if the possessor establishes evidence of birth, it will be accepted and the judgment for Zayd will be overtured. His statement 'And if the outsider establishes...': If the outsider (non-possessor) establishes evidence of absolute ownership and the possessor establishes that he bought from that outsider, then the possessor's evidence is considered, because the outsider is proving priority of ownership, and the possessor is proving acquisition from him, and there is no contradiction. So it is as if the possessor first acknowledged ownership for the outsider and then claimed purchase from him.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a ruling from Al-Hidayah regarding the priority of evidence when multiple parties claim ownership of a property. The opening line identifies the chapter on what two men claim (باب ما يدعيه الرجلان). The commentator explains the vocabulary, then translates the ruling. The core principle is that evidence of birth (نتاج) — meaning that the property was born from an animal or slave owned by the claimant — is considered stronger than evidence of absolute ownership (ملک مطلق). This is because birth evidence is like a definitive text (نص) that leaves no room for ijtihad, whereas absolute ownership claims are based on ijtihad. Therefore, if a person was defeated in a case of absolute ownership, they can later bring evidence of birth and overturn the previous judgment. The commentary then extends this analogy to non-repetitive causes of ownership like milking, cheese-making, etc., versus repetitive causes like building, planting, and cultivating. If there is doubt, experts are consulted; if even experts cannot decide, the original principle (judgment for the non-possessor) prevails. The passage also covers the scenario where a non-possessor claims absolute ownership and the possessor claims purchase from that non-possessor — here the possessor is preferred because the two claims are not contradictory; the possessor is essentially acknowledging the other's ownership and then claiming a transfer from him.

Key Terms
خارج (kharaj): Non-possessor; the person not in possession who claims ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario where a non-possessor claims absolute ownership and the possessor claims purchase from that non-possessor, whose evidence is accepted?
A) The non-possessor's
B) The possessor's
C) Both are accepted equally
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
When a possessor proves purchase from the non-possessor who claims ownership, the possessor prevails because the claims are compatible.

Conflicting Evidence of Purchase Without Dates: The Hanafi Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on conflicting purchase evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the disagreement between the Shaykhayn and Imam Muhammad on conflicting purchase evidence without dates and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
When two parties each prove purchase from each other without dates, the Shaykhayn nullify both; Muhammad gives effect to both.

When two parties each present evidence that they purchased the same property from each other, with no dates, how does a Hanafi qadi rule? This passage from Al-Hidayah presents a famous intra-madhhab dispute between the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. The ruling hinges on whether the act of claiming purchase inherently acknowledges the other's ownership, leading to mutual nullification (tahatur).

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the main ruling
Recognize that the case involves two parties each establishing evidence of purchasing the same property from each other, with no dates provided. Note the default ruling stated at the beginning.
The initial ruling is that both evidences are nullified and property remains with the current possessor.
2
Distinguish the two positions
Attribution: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (Shaykhayn) hold the initial ruling. Imam Muhammad holds that both evidences are given effect and property goes to the outsider (non-possessor).
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Analyze the reasoning (dalil) of each party
Shaykhayn: Initiating a purchase is an implicit acknowledgment of the seller's ownership, creating a mutual acknowledgment that nullifies both evidences by consensus. Muhammad: Both evidences can be acted upon by constructing a scenario where the possessor bought first, took possession, then sold without delivery (permissible in real property according to him).
The key difference is how the act of claiming purchase is interpreted.
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Under Shaykhayn, the property stays with the current possessor. Under Muhammad, it goes to the outsider.
This difference directly affects who wins the dispute in court.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the view of the Shaykhayn, as stated in the text and supported by later Hanafi authorities.
Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah presents the Shaykhayn's view as the main position.

الثَّمَنِ فَالْقِصَاصُ مَذْهَبُ مُحَمَّدٌ لِلْوُجُوبِ عِنْدَهُ وَلَوْ شَهِدَ الْفَرِيقَانِ بِالْبَيْعِ وَالْقَبْضِ تَهَاتَرَنَا بِالْإِجْمَاعِ لِأَنَّ الْجَمْعَ غَيْرُ مُمْكِن عِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٌ لِجَوَازِ كُلَّ وَاحِدٍ مِنَ الْبَيْعَيْنِ بِخِلَافِ الْاَوَّلِ وَإِنْ وَقَتَتِ الْبَيِّنَتَانِ فِي الْعِقَارِ وَلَمْ يَنْتَا قَبْضًا وَوَقْتُ الْخَارِج أَسْبَقُ يُقْضَى لِصَاحِبِ الْيَدِ عِنْدَهُمَا فَيُجْعَلُ كَأَنَّ الْخَارِجَ اشْتَرَى أَوَّلًا ثُمَّ بَاعَ قَبْلَ الْقَبْضِ مِنْ صَاحِبِ الْيَدِ وَهُوَ جَائِزٌ فِي الْعِقَارِ عِنْدَهُمَا وَعِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٌ يُقْضَى لِلْخَارِجِ لِأَنَّهُ لَا يَصِحُ بَيْعُهُ قَبْلَ الْقَبْضِ فَبَقِيَ عَلَى مِلْكِهِ وَإِنْ أَثْبَتَا قَبْضًا يُقْضَى لِصَاحِبِ الْيَدِ لِأَنَّ الْبَيْعَيْنِ جَائِزَانِ عَلَى الْقَوْلَيْنِ وَإِذَا كَانَ وَقْتُ صَاحِبِ الْيَدِ أَسْبَقُ يُقْضَى لِلْخَارِجِ فِي الْوَجْهَيْنِ فَيُجْعَلُ كَأَنَّهُ اشْتَرَاهُ ذُو الْيَدِ وَقَبْضَ ثُمَّ . بَاعَ وَلَمْ يُسَلَّمْ أَوْ سَلَّمَ ثُمَّ وَصَلَ إِلَيْهِ بِسَبَبٍ أَخَرَ
ترجمہ اگر پینہ قائم کی ان میں سے ہر ایک نے دوسرے سے خریدنے پر اور تاریخ دونوں کے پس نہیں تو ساقط ہوں گے۔ دونوں پیتے اور چھوڑ دیا جائے گا مکان قابض کے قبضہ میں۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں۔ کہ یہ شیخین کے نزدیک ہے۔ امام محمد کے قول میں دونوں بینوں پر حکم ہو گا۔ اور مال غیر قابض کے لئے ہوگا۔ کیونکہ دونوں پر عمل ممکن ہے۔ پس یوں قرار دیا جائے گا کہ گویا قابض نے دوسرے سے خریدا اور قبضہ کرلیا۔ پھر اسی کے ہاتھ بیچا اور قبضہ نہیں دیا۔ کیونکہ قبضہ دلیل سبقت ہے۔ جیسا کہ گذر چکا۔ اور اس کے برعکس نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ بیع قبل از قبض جائز نہیں۔ اگر چہ عقار میں ہو۔ امام محمد کے نزدیک شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ خرید پر اقدام کرنا اس کی طرف سے اقرار ہے۔ ملک بائع کا تو ایسا ہوگیا کہ گویا دونوں پہنے دونوں اقراروں پر قائم ہوئے ہیں۔ اور ایسی صورت میں ساقط ہوتا ہے۔ بالا جماع ایسے ہی یہاں ہو گا۔ اور اس لئے کہ سب کا اعتبار اس کے حکم کی وجہ سے ہوتا ہے اور وہ ملک ہے۔ اور یہاں قابض کے لئے حکم ممکن نہیں۔ مگر بملک مستحق تو قابض کے لئے حکم صرف سب کے ساتھ ہوا جو کچھ پھر پر تو یا مفید نہیں ۔ پھر اگر دونوں بینوں نے اداشمن پر گواہی دی۔ تو ہزار ہزار کے عوض با ہم بدلا ہو جائے گا۔ شیخین کے نزدیک جب کہ دونوں مساوی ہوں۔
Translation: If each of them establishes evidence of purchase from the other and there is no date with them, the two pieces of evidence are nullified and the house is left in the hand of the possessor. He (the author) said: This is according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. And according to the saying of Muhammad, judgment is given on both evidences and it goes to the outsider, because acting on both is possible. So it is considered as if the possessor bought from the other and took possession, then sold without delivery, because possession is an indication of precedence as passed. The matter is not reversed because sale before possession is not permissible even if in real property according to him. Their (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf's) argument is that proceeding to purchase is an acknowledgment by him of the seller's ownership, so it becomes as if both evidences were established on two acknowledgments, and in that case nullification is by consensus, so here too. And because the cause (sabab) is intended for its ruling, which is ownership, and here judgment for the possessor is not possible except with established ownership, so judgment for him remains only by the mere cause, which does not benefit him. Then if the two pieces of evidence testify to payment of the price, then one thousand against one thousand is set-off (qisas) according to them when they are equal, due to the existence of guaranteed possession from each side. And if they do not testify to payment of price, then set-off is the madhhab of Muhammad due to obligation according to him. And if the two groups testify to sale and possession, they nullify by consensus, because combination is impossible according to Muhammad... And if the two evidences are dated in real property and they do not prove possession, and the outsider's date is earlier, judgment is for the possessor according to them, so it is considered as if the outsider bought first then sold before possession to the possessor, which is permissible in real property according to them. According to Muhammad, judgment is for the outsider because his sale before possession is invalid, so it remains in his ownership. And if they prove possession, judgment is for the possessor because both sales are permissible on both sayings. And if the possessor's date is earlier, judgment is for the outsider in both ways, so it is considered as if the possessor bought and took possession, then sold without delivery or delivered then it reached him by another cause.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed intra-Hanafi dispute regarding conflicting evidence when two parties each claim to have purchased the same property from each other, but neither provides a date. The text first states the ruling that the evidences are mutually nullified (تهاترت البينتان) and the property remains with the current possessor (ذي اليد). This is attributed to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the Shaykhayn). Then Imam Muhammad's view is given: both evidences are given effect, and the property is awarded to the outsider (non-possessor) because it is possible to act on both. He constructs a scenario: the possessor bought from the outsider, took possession, then sold it back without delivery. This is permissible because the possession of the first buyer proves his prior ownership. The Shaykhayn's counter-argument is that initiating a purchase is an implicit acknowledgment of the seller's ownership, so both parties are acknowledging each other's ownership, leading to nullification by consensus. They also argue that the cause (sabab) is only valid if it leads to its intended effect (ownership), but here the possessor cannot be awarded ownership except through a valid ownership chain. The passage then extends the discussion to scenarios where the witnesses also testify to payment of price (nagd al-thaman), leading to set-off (qisas) if equal and if the price was paid. Muhammad's view on set-off is noted. Further, if both parties testify to sale and possession, the evidences are nullified by consensus because it's impossible for both to be true simultaneously. The text also discusses cases with dates in real property ( عقار) and possession, with differences between Shaykhayn and Muhammad. The Urdu commentary summarizes and clarifies the arguments.

Key Terms
تهاتر البينتان (tahatara al-bayyinatan): Mutual nullification of two conflicting pieces of evidence, i.e., both are disregarded.
ذي اليد (dhi al-yad): The person in possession of the property in dispute.
قصاص (qisas): Set-off; here used for mutual cancellation of debt when both sides claim payment of the same amount.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, if two parties each claim to have purchased the same house from each other with no dates, what happens to the property?
A) It is divided equally
B) It goes to the outside claimant
C) Both evidences are nullified and the property stays with the current possessor
D) It goes to the one who first established evidence

Key Takeaway
In conflicting purchase evidence without dates, the Hanafi mufta bihi nullifies both pieces of evidence and leaves the property with the current possessor.

Qada — Judiciary
beginner

House in Both Hands: Ruling for All-Claimant
Ruling when a house is in both hands and one claims all

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a house is in the possession of both claimants and one claims the entire house, and explain why half is given by judicial decree and half remains without decree.

Core Idea
What is unclaimed remains with the possessor without judicial decree.

In disputes over jointly possessed property, the judge only intervenes where there is a claim. This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies a specific scenario: when a house is held by both parties and one claimant asserts full ownership, the judge decrees half of the house based on evidence, while the half already in the claimant's possession remains with him without a decree because it is not claimed by the other. This rule hinges on the principle that judicial decree requires a claim.

Guided Path
1
Identify the factual scenario
The house is in the possession of both claimants. One claimant asserts that the entire house belongs to him.
Possession is shared; claim is for all.
2
Distinguish the two halves
Half of the house is in the other party's possession (the half not in the claimant's hand). The other half is in the claimant's own hand.
The phrase 'kharij (outsider)' indicates the claimant is an outsider to the half in the other's hand.
3
Apply the principle of claim and evidence
For the half not in his possession, the claimant has evidence, so the judge gives a decree for that half based on his evidence.
Judgment is only on the half that is claimed and not in his hand.
4
Apply the principle 'no judgment without claim'
The half already in his possession is not claimed by the other party, so no judicial decree is needed; it remains his without a formal judgment.
If the other party had claimed that half, a decree would be necessary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَلَوْ كَانَتْ فِي أَيْدِيهِمَا سَلَّمَ لِصَاحِبِ الْجَمِيعِ نِصْفَهَا عَلَى وَجْهِ الْقَضَاءِ وَنِصْفَهَا لَا عَلَى وَجْهِ الْقَضَاءِ لِأَنَّهُ خَارِجٌ فِي النِّصْفِ فَيُقْضَى بَيِّنَتِهِ وَالنِّصْفُ الَّذِى فِى يَدَيْهِ صَاحِبُهُ لَا يَدَّعِيهِ لاَنَّ مُدَّعَاهُ النِّصْفُ وَهُوَ فِي يَدِهِ سَالِمٌ لَهُ وَلَوْ لَمْ يَنْصَرِفْ إِلَيْهِ دَعْوَاهُ كَانَ ظَالِمًا بِإِمْسَاكِهِ وَلَا قَضَاءَ بِدُونِ الدَّعْوَى فَيُتْرَكُ فِي يَدِهِ
He said: And if it (the house) is in both their hands, he gives to the claimant of all half of it by way of judicial decree (qada) and half of it not by way of judicial decree, because he is an outsider (kharij) regarding the half, so judgment is given on his evidence; and the half that is in his own hand, no one claims it from him, because his claim is only for the half and it is in his hand safe for him. And if his claim does not extend to it, he would be unjust in retaining it, and there is no judgment without a claim, so it is left in his hand.
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage addresses a scenario where the house is in the possession of both claimants. The all-claimant gets a judgment for half of the house because that half is not in his possession but he has evidence for it. The other half is already in his possession and not claimed by the other party, so it remains with him without the need for a judicial decree. The rationale is that judgment requires a claim; since no one claims the half in his own hand, it remains his without formal decree.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada): Judicial decree by a qadi (judge)
دعوى (da'wa): Claim or lawsuit

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a house is in the hands of both claimants and one claims the entire house, what happens to the half in his own hand?
A) It is given to the other claimant.
B) It is divided equally.
C) It remains with him without judicial decree.
D) The case is dismissed.

Key Takeaway
A judicial decree is only required for property that is claimed by another; unclaimed possession remains with the possessor.

Resolving Ownership Claims with Dated Witnesses
Ruling on evidence priority with dated witnesses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on an animal dispute with dated witnesses and apply the three possible outcomes based on the animal's age relative to the dates.

Core Idea
The animal's age compared to witnesses' dates decides ownership: match one → that claimant; match both → shared; contradict both → left with possessor.

When two people each bring witnesses and dates claiming ownership of an animal, the judge uses the animal's age as a decisive clue. This ruling from Al-Hidayah provides a clear hierarchy: age matching one date gives the animal to that claimant; if both dates match or cannot be determined, the animal is shared; if both dates are contradicted, the witnesses are disbelieved and the current possessor keeps it. Understanding this shows how Hanafi qada combines circumstantial evidence (zahir hal) with the integrity of testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute components
Two claimants each present witnesses (bayyinah) and state a date (tārīkh) for their transaction. The animal's current age is known.
The date is when the claimant supposedly acquired the animal.
2
Compare the animal's age with each date
Determine if the animal's age matches one date, both dates, or neither. Age matching means the animal was born (or is old enough) consistent with the claimed time of acquisition.
For example, if the animal is 5 years old and one witness says it was acquired 5 years ago, that date matches.
3
Apply the ruling based on the comparison
If age matches one date only → that claimant gets the animal. If age matches both dates or cannot be determined → the animal is shared equally. If age contradicts both dates → both witnesses are deemed false and the animal remains with the current possessor.
The reasoning: matching age makes the zahir hal (apparent situation) a witness; contradiction exposes falsity.
4
Understand the basis in evidence theory
The ruling balances the probative value of testimony against objective facts. A date that aligns with the animal's age strengthens the claim; a date that conflicts weakens it. When both conflict, the testimonies are mutually contradictory and thus rejected.
This reflects the Hanafi principle that bayyinah must be consistent with common sense (qiyas).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ما يدعيه الرجلان ۲۸ ایک نے غصب کا اور دوسرے نے ودیعت کا تو غلام دونوں میں مساوی ہوگا۔ کیونکہ وہ دونوں برابر ہیں۔ یہ جلد - یازدهم تشریح قوله واذا تنازعا...... دو آدمیوں نے ایک جانور کی بابت جھگڑا کیا اور دونوں نے اپنی اپنی ملکہ [؟] تنازع پر بینہ قائم کیا اور دونوں نے تاریخ بھی بیان کر دی تو اس کی عمر جس کی تاریخ کے موافق ہو جانور اسی کو دلایا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ ظاہر حال اسی کے حق میں شاہد ہے۔ اور اگر ان کی بیان کردہ تاریخوں کے لحاظ سے اس کی عمر کا پتہ چلانا مشکل ہو تو جانور دونوں کا مشترک رہے گا۔ لان احدها ليس باولى بها منالاخر - اور اگر دابہ کی عمر ان دونوں تاریخوں سے مخالف ہو تو بینے باطل ہوں گے۔ جیسا کہ حاکم شہید نے ذکر کیا ہے۔ کیونکہ دونوں بینوں کا کذب ظاہر ہو گیا۔ پس وہ جانور جس کے قبضہ میں ہے اس کے قبضہ میں چھوڑا جائے گا۔ شیخ ابواللیث خوارزمی کی روایت میں بھی یونہی ہے۔
Section: What two men claim. 28. One made a claim of usurpation and the other of deposit, so the slave is shared equally between them because they are equal. This is volume 11. Explanation of his saying: 'And when they dispute...' Two men disputed about an animal, and both established evidence for their ownership and also gave a date. Then if the animal's age matches the date of one of them, the animal will be given to that one because the apparent situation is a witness for him. If determining the age according to their dates is difficult, the animal remains shared between them because neither has priority over the other. If the animal's age contradicts both dates, both evidences are invalid, as mentioned by Hakim Shahid, because the falsity of both evidences becomes apparent. Then the animal is left with the one in whose possession it is. The narration of Shaykh Abul Layth Khwarizmi is also like this.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a ruling from Al-Hidayah regarding disputes over an animal when both claimants produce witnesses with dates. The ruling establishes a hierarchy: first, if the animal's age corresponds to one date, that claimant prevails based on circumstantial evidence. If both dates match the age, the animal is shared equally. If both dates conflict with the age, the witnesses are disbelieved and the animal remains with the current possessor. The commentary notes that this is also the view in the narration of Shaykh Abul Layth. The initial line about ghasb and wadi‘a is a reference to a separate ruling that will follow.

Key Terms
بینہ (bayyinah): Legal evidence, typically testimony of witnesses.
تاریخ (tārīkh): Date provided by the witness regarding the transaction.
دابہ (dābbah): A riding animal, such as a horse or camel.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Two claimants each present witnesses with dates for a camel. The camel's age matches only the first claimant's date. According to the Hanafi ruling, what is the outcome?
A) The camel is shared equally between them.
B) The camel goes to the first claimant.
C) The camel goes to the second claimant.
D) The camel is left with the current possessor.

Key Takeaway
In an ownership dispute with dated witnesses, the animal's age determines priority: match one claimant gets it, match both or unclear means sharing, contradict both means the possessor keeps it.

Dispute between Claim of Ghasb and Wadi'a: Equal Division
Ruling on split ownership when one claims ghasb and the other wadi'a

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when two claimants present conflicting evidence (ghasb vs wadi'a) and apply it to similar cases.

Core Idea
When two claimants each bring evidence, one for usurpation and one for deposit, the property is divided equally between them.

Two people claim ownership of property in the hands of a third party. Amr says the possessor is a usurper; Bakr says he is a depositee. The Hanafi school rules that they are equal in claim, so the property is split half and half. This ruling from Al-Hidayah highlights a unique judicial approach when both claims are equally supported by evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and property
Zayd is the possessor of a slave (or similar property). Amr claims that Zayd wrongfully took it (ghasb), and Bakr claims that he gave it to Zayd as a deposit (wadi'a). Both bring valid evidence (bayyinah).
The property is a tangible, divisible asset.
2
Recognize the conflict
The claims are contradictory: ghasb implies theft, while wadi'a implies lawful possession. The same property cannot be both usurped and deposited at the same time from different owners.
The contradiction lies in the legal status of Zayd's possession.
3
Apply the ruling
Since both claimants provide evidence, they are considered equal. The qadi does not favor one over the other; instead, the property is divided equally between Amr and Bakr.
The ruling applies only when both claims are proven with valid evidence.
4
Understand the legal reason (talil)
The text offers a reason: 'al-wadi'a tasiru ghasban bil-juhud' (the deposit becomes usurpation by denial). This means a depositee who denies the deposit becomes liable like a usurper. Here, the principle underpins that both claims are treated with equal weight because the evidence is balanced.
The reason is not directly about the claimants but about the nature of deposit when denied.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله واذا كان العبد ایک چیز (غلام وغیرہ) زید کے قبضہ میں ہے۔ عمرو نے اس کی بابت بینہ قائم کیا کہ قابض نے یہ مجھ سے چھین لی ہے۔ اور بکر نے بینہ سے یہ ثابت کیا کہ میں نے یہ چیز قابض کو بطور امانت دی ہے تو وہ دونوں اپنے اپنے دعوی میں برابر ہوں گے۔ اور وہ چیز کسی ایک کو نہ دلائی جائے گی۔ بلکہ ان میں نصف نصف کر دی جائے گی۔ لان الوديعة تصير غصباً بالجحود حتى يجب عليه الضمان
His saying: 'And when a slave...': A thing (a slave or similar) is in Zayd's possession. Amr establishes evidence that the possessor usurped it from him, and Bakr establishes evidence that he gave it to the possessor as a deposit. Then they are equal in their claims, and the thing will not be given to either alone, but will be divided half and half between them because the deposit becomes usurpation by denial such that liability is established.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This is a commentary on a ruling from Al-Hidayah. The scenario: Zayd has a slave. Amr claims Zayd wrongfully took it (ghasb) and Bakr claims he gave it to Zayd as a deposit (wadi‘a). Both provide witnesses. Since the claim of deposit is effectively an admission that the property was in Zayd's possession lawfully, while the claim of ghasb implies wrongful possession, they contradict. The ruling is that neither claimant is preferred, so the property is split equally between them. The reason given: a deposit becomes a usurpation if the depositee denies it (i.e., if the depositee claims it as his own, it becomes a usurpation, but here the depositee is not the claimant; it's a third party. The meaning: the one claiming deposit is essentially admitting that the possessor had the thing, so his claim is weaker; nevertheless, they are treated equally.)

Key Terms
غصب (ghasb): Wrongful appropriation or usurpation of another's property.
ودیعت (wadī‘at): A deposit; property entrusted to someone for safekeeping without compensation.
بینہ (bayyinah): Evidence; here, the testimony of two male witnesses or one male and two females.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a dispute where two claimants present evidence: one claims ghasb, the other claims wadi'a, what is the Hanafi ruling according to Al-Hidayah?
A) The property is awarded to the ghasb claimant.
B) The property is awarded to the wadi'a claimant.
C) The property is divided equally.
D) The property remains with the possessor.

Key Takeaway
When two claimants each present evidence, one for usurpation and one for deposit, the Hanafi ruling is equal division between them.

Resolving Possession Disputes: The Principle of Apparent Control
Rules for resolving disputes based on apparent physical possession indicators

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of apparent possession (tasarruf) to resolve disputes over movable property by identifying the more dominant physical control.

Core Idea
Apparent control (tasarruf) decides ownership in disputes, not mere physical contact.

In Islamic courts, when two claimants dispute ownership and neither has proof, the Hanafi school relies on apparent possession indicators. This section from Al-Hidayah presents several common scenarios—riding an animal, wearing a garment, holding a rein—and the ruling follows a simple but powerful principle: the person whose action shows more dominant control has priority. Understanding these rules equips the student with a clear methodology for adjudicating such disputes in the absence of evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed object and claimants' actions
For each scenario in the text, note what the item is (animal, garment, carpet) and precisely what each claimant is doing (riding, holding rein, sitting, etc.).
The text lists six scenarios; we will examine each in order.
2
Apply the principle of apparent control
Determine whose action (tasarruf) is more closely associated with ownership. Riding is more controlling than holding a rein; wearing is more controlling than holding a sleeve; loading is more controlling than hanging a jug.
The reasoning 'li anna tasarrufahu azhar' (because his control is more apparent) is the key proof.
3
Derive the ruling
State who gets the item: rider over rein-holder, saddle rider over pillion, load owner over jug owner, wearer over sleeve-holder. For equal control (two riders, sitter vs. holder of carpet, part-in-hand), the item is shared.
Two riders share because both have equal control (istiwā' fī al-tasarruf).
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the saddle rider
The text gives priority to the saddle rider based on a narration from Nawadir Mu‘alla. In Zahir al-Riwayah (the core Hanafi texts), both riders share equally. Identify the difference and its authority.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school; the mufta bihi may vary.
5
Evaluate the underlying proof
The proof is the principle that dominant possession indicates ownership. This is a form of istidlāl (reasoning) based on observable practice, not a textual source. Confirm the logic: why does riding show more ownership than holding a rein?
The text says 'al-rukūb yakhtaṣṣu bi al-milk' (riding is specific to ownership).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

مَعْنَاهُ لَا عَلَى طَرِيقِ الْقَضَاءِ لِاَنَّ الْقُعُودَ لَيْسَ بِيَدٍ عَلَيْهِ فَاسْتَوَيَا قَالَ وَإِذَا كَانَ ثَوْبٌ فِي يَدِ رَجُلٍ وَطَرَتْ مِنْهُ فِي يَدٍ آخَرَ فَهُوَ بَيْنَهُمَا نِصْفَانِ کے بعد اس ملک کا بیان ہے جو ظاہری قبضہ سے ہوتی ہے۔ اور اوّل کو اس لئے مقدم کیا ہے کہ وہ قوی تر ہے۔ یہاں تک کہ جب بینہ قائم ہو جائے تو پھر ظاہری قبضہ کی طرف کوئی التفات نہیں ہوتی۔ قوله تنازعاً فى دابة ... زید ایک گھوڑے پر سوار ہے اور عمر و اس کے لگام پکڑے ہوئے ہے۔ یازید زین پر سوار ہے اور عمرو اس کا ردیف ہے۔ یا اونٹ پر زید کا بوجھ لدا ہوا ہے اور عمرہ کا آنجورہ اس پر لٹکا ہوا ہے۔ یا زید گرتا پہنے ہوئے ہے اور عمرو اس کی آستینیں پکڑے ہوئے۔ اب گھوڑے یا اونٹ گرتے میں دونوں کا جھگڑا ہوا۔ زید کہتاہ کی میرا ہے اور عمرو کہتا ہے کہ میرا ہے تو گھوڑایا اونٹ یا گر تا زید ہی کا ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس کا تصرف ظاہر تر ہے۔ لان الركوب واللبس يختصان ب الملك۔ پھر رکوپ دابہ والا مسئلہ ائمہ اربعہ کے یہاں متفق علیہ ہے۔ اور راکب سرج کا اولیٰ ہونا اس روایت پر مبنی ہے۔ جس کو شیخ ناطفی نے اجناس میں نو وادر معلے سے نقل کیا ہے۔ ظاہر الروایہ میں وہ جانور دونوں میں نصف نصف ہو گا۔ (غایہ ، عنایہ ) قوله اذا كان ثوب .... ایک کپڑا کسی کے قبضہ میں ہے اور اس کا کنارہ دوسرے کے ہاتھ میں ہے۔ تو وہ ان میں نصف نصف ہوگا۔ کیونکہ جس کے ہاتھ میں زیادہ حصہ ہے۔ وہ بھی گرفت کی محبت ہے تو اس سے کچھ زیادہ استحقاق ثابت نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ علت کی کثرت سے ترجیح نہیں ہوتی ۔
Section on disputes concerning possession. Translation: This section explains dispute regarding possession. Two men disputed about a quadruped: one is riding it and the other is holding its rein, so the rider has priority. He said: And when they dispute about an animal, one of them riding it and the other holding its rein, then the rider has priority because his control is more apparent; indeed, riding is specific to ownership. Likewise, if one of them is sitting in the saddle and the other is his pillion rider, then the one in the saddle has priority, contrary to when both are riding, in which case it is shared between them due to equality of control. Likewise, if they dispute about a camel with a load belonging to one of them and the other has a water jug hanging from it, then the owner of the load has priority because he is the one acting. Likewise, if they dispute about a garment, one of them wearing it and the other holding its sleeve, then the wearer has priority because his control is more apparent. If they dispute about a carpet, one sitting on it and the other holding it, then it is shared between them, meaning not by way of judicial decision, because sitting is not possession; so they are equal. He said: And if a cloth is in the hand of a man and a part of it is in the hand of another, then it is half and half between them because the increase is of the same genus as the evidence, so it does not necessitate an increase in entitlement. Vocabulary explanation... (Urdu translation follows)... Commentary on his saying: The section after the explanation of ownership by proof, now explains ownership by apparent possession. The first is preferred because it is stronger. Until when evidence is established, then no attention is paid to apparent possession. His saying: Dispute over an animal... (Urdu examples)... Then the issue of riding an animal is agreed upon by the four Imams. The priority of the rider in the saddle is based on a narration that Shaykh al-Natiﬁ transmitted from Nawadir Mu‘alla. In Zahir al-Riwayah, the animal is shared half and half. (Ghayla, ‘Inaya)...
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This is a detailed section from Al-Hidayah on resolving disputes through apparent possession. The general principle: the person who exercises more visible control (riding, wearing, loading) is preferred. The Arabic matn lists several scenarios: a rider vs. rein-holder (rider wins), saddle rider vs. pillion (saddle rider wins), two riders (shared), camel with load vs. hanging jug (load owner wins), shirt wearer vs. sleeve holder (wearer wins), carpet sitter vs. holder (shared because sitting is not possession), cloth one hand vs. another (shared because extra grip is not extra proof). The commentary notes that the riding case is agreed upon by all four schools, but the saddle rider's priority is based on a nawadir narration; in Zahir al-Riwayah, both riders share equally. The later commentary elaborates on the comparison between ownership by proof and by possession.

Key Terms
راکب (rākib): The person riding the animal; in the text, the rider has more apparent control.
لجام (lijām): The rein of the animal, held by the other claimant.
ردیف (radīf): A pillion rider sitting behind the main rider.
تصرف (taṣarruf): Control or use of property; the more apparent control indicates ownership.
بساط (bisāṭ): A carpet or spread; sitting on it is not considered possession.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a dispute over a camel, one person has a load on the camel and the other has a water jug hanging from it. Who gets the camel?
A) The person with the water jug.
B) The person with the load.
C) Both share the camel.
D) The camel goes to the possessor.

Key Takeaway
In possession disputes without evidence, the Hanafi school prioritizes the claimant whose apparent control (tasarruf) is more dominant, sharing only when control is equal.

Determining a Child's Freedom or Slavery Based on Ability to Speak
Rules for determining legal status of a child in possession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rules for a child's legal status when found in someone's possession, and apply the criterion of ta‘bīr ‘an al-nafs to determine whether the child's declaration is legally effective.

Core Idea
A child's ability to express himself determines whether his declaration of freedom or slavery is accepted.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a specific legal problem: when a child is found in someone's possession, how do we determine if he is free or a slave? The key factor is the child's capacity to speak and make a coherent claim. The Hanafi school provides clear rules based on whether the child can express himself and what he says.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key criterion
The child's ability to express himself (yu‘abbiru ‘an nafsihi) is the central factor. If he can speak coherently, his statement has legal effect. If not, he is treated like chattel.
2
Ruling when child claims freedom
If the child says 'I am free,' his statement is accepted, and he is considered free because he is in his own hand (i.e., he has self-possession).
This applies only if he can express himself.
3
Ruling when child claims slavery
If the child says 'I am a slave of so-and-so,' he becomes a slave of that person. By admitting slavery, he acknowledges that he has no self-ownership.
The current possessor does not automatically own him; he belongs to the named person.
4
Ruling when child cannot speak
If the child cannot express himself, he is considered a slave of the person in whose hand he is, because he has no self-possession. He is like a chattel (متاع).
This is a default ruling based on possession.
5
Consequence after adulthood
If slavery was established in childhood (either by his statement or by inability to speak), later claiming freedom as an adult is not accepted. The prior status is considered proven.
This prevents later disputes from overturning an established legal fact.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَإِذَا كَانَ الصَّبِيُّ فِي يَدِ رَجُلٍ وَهُوَ يُعَبِّرُ عَنْ نَفْسِهِ فَقَالَ أَنَا حُرِّ فَالْقَوْلُ قَوْلُهُ لِأَنَّهُ فِي يَدِ نَفْسِهِ وَلَوْ قَالَ أَنَا عَبْدٌ لِفُلان فَهُوَ عَبْدَ لِلَّذِي فِي يَدِهِ لأَنَّهُ أَقَرَّ بأنَّهُ لَا يَدَ لَهُ حَيْثُ أَفَرَّ بالرَقِ وَإِنْ كَانَ لَا يُعَبِّرُ عَنْ نَفْسِهِ فَهُوَ عَبْدٌ لِلَّذِي هُوَ فِي يَدِهِ لِأَنَّهُ لَا يَدَ لَهُ عَلَى نَفْسِهِ لِمَا كَانَ لَا يُعَبِّرُ عَنْهَا وَهُوَ بِمَنْزِلَةِ مَتَاعِ بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا كَانَ يُعَبِّرُ فَلَوْ كَبِرَ وَادَّعَى الْحُرِّيَّةَ لَا يَكُونُ الْقَوْلُ قَوْلَهُ لِأَنَّهُ ظَهَرَ الرَّقُ عَلَيْهِ فِي حَالِ صَغَرِهِ ترجمہ اگر بچہ کسی کے قبضہ میں ہو۔ در آنحالیکہ وہ اپنی ذات سے تعبیر کر سکتا ہے۔ پس اس نے کہا کہ میں آزاد ہوں تو اس کا قول معتبر ہو گا۔ کیونکہ وہ اپنے ذاتی قبضہ میں ہے۔ اور اگر اس نے کہا کہ میں فلاں کا غلام ہوں تو وہ اس کا غلام ہو گا جس کے قبضہ میں ہے۔ اور اگر وہ اپنی ذات سے تعبیر نہیں کر سکتا تو وہ اس کا غلام ہوگا۔ جس کے قبضہ میں وہ ہے کیونکہ اس کا اپنا ذاتی قبضہ نہیں ہے۔ بایں معنی کہ وہ اپنی ذات سے تعبیر نہیں کر سکتا تو وہ بمنزلہ اسباب کے ہے بخلاف اس کے جب وہ تعبیر کر سکتا ہو۔ پھر اگر وہ بالغ ہو کر آزادی کا دعوے کرے تب بھی اس کا قول معتبر نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ صغر سنی میں اس پر رقیت ظاہر ہو چکی۔
He said: And when a boy is in the hand of a man and he can express himself, and says 'I am free,' then his statement is accepted because he is in his own hand. If he says 'I am a slave of so-and-so,' then he is a slave of the one in whose hand he is because he has admitted that he has no hand over himself, having admitted to slavery. If he cannot express himself, then he is a slave of the one in whose hand he is because he has no hand over himself since he cannot express himself, and he is like a chattel, contrary to when he can express. Then if he grows up and claims freedom, his statement is not accepted because slavery was apparent upon him in childhood. Translation: If a child is in someone's possession, and he can express himself, and he says 'I am free,' then his statement is accepted because he is in his own possession. If he says 'I am the slave of so-and-so,' then he is the slave of the one in whose hand he is. If he cannot express himself, then he is the slave of the one in whose hand he is because he has no possession of himself, meaning he cannot express, so he is like a chattel, contrary to when he can express. Then if he becomes adult and claims freedom, his statement is still not accepted because slavery was apparent upon him in childhood.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This is a definition ruling from Al-Hidayah about the legal status of a child (ṣabī) in someone's possession. The key criterion: the child's ability to express himself (yu‘abbiru ‘an nafsihi). If the child can speak and declares himself free, his statement is accepted, and he is considered free, because he is in his own hand (i.e., he controls himself). If he declares himself a slave of a particular person, then he is considered a slave of that person, because by admitting slavery he admits he has no self-ownership. If he cannot express himself, then he is a slave of the person who holds him, because he lacks self-ownership and is like chattel. Once slavery is established in childhood, later claiming freedom as an adult is not accepted because the prior status of slavery is considered proven. The Urdu translation clarifies these rules.

Key Terms
صبی (ṣabī): A minor child who has not reached puberty.
تعبیر عن النفس (ta‘bīr ‘an al-nafs): The ability to express oneself coherently, including the ability to claim freedom or slavery.
رق (riqq): Slavery; the state of being a slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a child who can speak says 'I am a slave of so-and-so,' what is the ruling?
A) He is considered free until proven otherwise.
B) He becomes the slave of the person he named.
C) He remains with the current possessor as a free person.
D) The case is deferred until adulthood.

Key Takeaway
A child's ability to express himself is decisive: if he can speak, his statement is accepted; if not, he is deemed a slave of his possessor, and later claims of freedom are not accepted.

Establishing Possession of Land: Evidence vs. Overt Acts
Ruling on land possession with evidence and tasarruf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for resolving land possession disputes and apply it to scenarios with and without evidence.

Core Idea
Land possession is not presumed; evidence or visible use (tasarruf) is required to establish it before a judge.

When two people claim the same piece of land, the judge cannot simply assume who holds it. Possession of land is not observable like movable property. The Hanafi school provides a clear procedure: the claimant must bring evidence or demonstrate overt acts of ownership. This lesson explains the ruling and its practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
Two individuals each claim possession of a specific piece of land. The judge hears their claims.
The text begins with 'When two men claim land'.
2
Evaluate the need for evidence
Since land possession is not directly observable (ghayr mushahadah), the judge cannot rule based on claims alone. Both must provide evidence (bayyinah) that the land is in their possession.
Principle: 'Whatever is absent from the judge's knowledge, evidence establishes it.'
3
Apply the evidence rule
If only one brings evidence, he is awarded exclusive possession. If both bring evidence, the land is placed in joint possession (both are considered possessors).
Possession is a sought right (haqq maqsud), and proof (hujjah) establishes it.
4
Consider overt acts (tasarruf)
If one claimant has performed visible acts of ownership—laying bricks, building, digging a well—these establish possession without the need for witnesses, because tasarruf is stronger than mere yad.
Tasarruf includes any physical use or development of the land.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَإِذَا ادَّعَى الرَّجُلَانِ أَرْضًا يَعْنِي يَدَّعِي كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِّنْهُمَا أَنَّهَا فِي يَدِهِ لَمْ يُقْضَ أَنَّهَا فِي يَدِ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا حَتَّى يُقِيمَا الْبَيِّنَةَ أَنَّهَا فِي أَيْدِيهِمَا لاَنَّ الْيَدَ فِيْهَا غَيْرَ مُشَاهَدَةٍ لِتَعَذُرٍ إِحْضَارِهَا وَمَا غَابَ عَنْ عِلْمِ الْقَاضِي فَالْبَيِّنَةُ تُثْبِتُهُ وَإِنْ أَقَامَ اَحَدُهُمَا الْبَيِّنَةَ جُعِلَتْ فِي يَدِهِ لِقِيَامِ الْحُجَّةِ لِأَنَّ الْيَدِ حَقٌّ مَقْصُودٌ وَإِنْ أَقَامَا الْبَيِّنَةَ جُعِلَتْ فِي أَيْدِيهِمَا لِمَا بَيَّنَّا فَلَا تُسْتَحِقُ لِأَحَدِهِمَا بِغَيْرِ حُجَّةٍ وَإِنْ كَانَ اَحَدُهُمَا قَدْ لَبْنَ فِي الْأَرْضِ أَوْ بَني أَوْ حَفَرَ فَهِيَ فِي يَدِهِ لِوُجُودِ التَّصَرُّفِ وَالْإِسْتِعْمَالِ فِيهَا
ترجمہ جب دعویٰ کیا دو نے زمین کا۔ یعنی ان میں سے ہر ایک نے دعوے کیا کہ وہ میرے قبضہ میں ہے۔ تو حکم نہیں کیا جائے گا کہ وہ ان میں سے کسی کے قبضہ میں ہے یہاں تک کہ دشواری کی وجہ سے اور جو چیز علم قاضی سے غائب ہو اس کو بینہ ہی ثابت کرے گا۔ اگر ان میں سے ایک نے بینہ قائم کیا تو اسی کے قبضہ میں کر دی جائے گی۔ قیام محبت کی وجہ سے کیونکہ قبضہ بھی ایک مقصود حق ہے اور اگر دونوں نے بینہ قائم کر دیا تو دونوں کے قبضہ میں قرار دی جائے گی۔ اُسی وجہ سے جو ہم نے بیان کی۔ پس بلا حجت کسی ایک کے لئے استحقاق کا حکم نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ اور اگر اُن میں سے ایک نے زمین میں اینٹ لگائی یا عمارت بنائی یا کنواں کھودا تو زمین اسی کے قبضہ میں ہوگی۔ تصرف اور استعمال پائے جانے کی وجہ سے۔
He said: And when two men claim land, meaning each of them claims that it is in his possession, it is not judged that it is in the possession of one of them until they bring evidence that it is in their possession. Because the possession (yad) in land is not visible (mushahadah) due to difficulty in presenting it, and whatever is absent from the knowledge of the judge, evidence (bayyinah) establishes it. And if one of them brings evidence, it is placed in his possession because proof stands; for possession is a right that is sought. And if both bring evidence, it is placed in their possession (jointly) for the reason we have explained. So it is not awarded to one of them without proof. And if one of them has laid bricks in the land, or built, or dug a well, then it is in his possession due to the existence of disposition (tasarruf) and use in it. Translation: When two men claim land, i.e., each claims it is in his possession, the judge does not rule that it is in the possession of either until they show evidence that it is in their possession, because possession of land is not witnessed (due to difficulty in producing it), and whatever is hidden from the judge's knowledge, only evidence proves it. If one of them establishes evidence, the land is placed in his possession, due to the establishment of proof, because possession is a desired right. And if both establish evidence, it is placed in both their possession, for the reason we have explained. So without proof, entitlement is not judged for either. And if one of them has laid bricks, built a structure, or dug a well, then the land is in his possession, due to the existence of disposition and use in it.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling on how a judge should resolve a dispute over land when two people each claim possession (yad). The passage is a ruling statement. The key point: land possession is not immediately apparent (ghayr mushahadah), so the judge requires evidence (bayyinah). If only one provides evidence, he is awarded possession. If both provide evidence, they share possession. Additionally, overt acts of construction or digging (tasarruf) establish possession without evidence, because they constitute visible use. The ruling ensures that possession is not granted arbitrarily but on the basis of proof or visible acts. The Hanafi principle here is that yad is a right that must be established, and the judge cannot assume possession without evidence.

Key Terms
يد (yad): Possession or control over property; in this context, actual physical possession as a legal basis for ownership.
بينة (bayyinah): Evidence, typically testimony of two witnesses, but may include other forms of proof.
تصرف (tasarruf): Disposition or act of using the property, like building, digging, etc. Evidence of possession.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if both claimants bring evidence that the land is in their possession?
A) The land is awarded to the one with stronger evidence.
B) The land is divided equally between them.
C) The land is placed in both their possession.
D) The case is dismissed.

Key Takeaway
In land disputes, possession (yad) is not presumed; evidence (bayyinah) or overt acts (tasarruf) are required to establish it before a judge.

Claiming Land Not in Visible Possession
Rulings on proof of land possession when physical control is absent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for land possession disputes when neither party has visible control, and apply the conditions of evidence (bayyinah) or physical disposition (tasarruf) to determine possession.

Core Idea
When land possession is invisible, the judge relies on evidence or physical acts to decide.

This lesson addresses a common scenario in property disputes: two claimants both assert possession of a piece of land, but the land cannot be physically brought to court. How does the qadi resolve this? The Hanafi school outlines clear rules: without visible yad, evidence is required. However, physical acts like building or digging are treated as evidence of possession.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial problem
Two claimants, each claims the land is in his possession, but neither can demonstrate visible yad. The judge cannot simply rule for one without proof.
Yad means actual physical control, which is not observable here.
2
Apply the general rule: evidence required
The judge does not rule for either until they present evidence (bayyinah) that the land is in their possession. Since possession is absent from the judge's knowledge, evidence establishes it.
Bayyinah typically means testimony of two male witnesses.
3
Apply the exceptions based on evidence or tasarruf
If only one provides evidence, the land is placed in his hand. If both provide evidence, it is placed in both their hands. If one has performed tasarruf (e.g., placed bricks, built, or dug), that act alone establishes possession in his hand, even without separate witnesses.
Tasarruf is a physical act of disposition indicating control.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَإِذَا ادَّعَى الرَّجُلَانِ أَرْضًا يَعْنِي يَدَّعِي كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِّنْهُمَا أَنَّهَا فِي يَدِهِ لَمْ يُقْضَ أَنَّهَا فِي يَدِ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا حَتَّى يُقِيمَا الْبَيِّنَةَ أَنَّهَا فِي أَيْدِيهِمَا لاَنَّ الْيَدَ فِيْهَا غَيْرَ مُشَاهَدَةٍ لِتَعَذُرٍ إِحْضَارِهَا وَمَا غَابَ عَنْ عِلْمِ الْقَاضِي فَالْبَيِّنَةُ تُثْبِتُهُ وَإِنْ أَقَامَ اَحَدُهُمَا الْبَيِّنَةَ جُعِلَتْ فِي يَدِهِ لِقِيَامِ الْحُجَّةِ لِأَنَّ الْيَدِ حَقٌّ مَقْصُودٌ وَإِنْ أَقَامَا الْبَيِّنَةَ جُعِلَتْ فِي أَيْدِيهِمَا لِمَا بَيَّنَّا فَلَا تُسْتَحِقُ لِأَحَدِهِمَا بِغَيْرِ حُجَّةٍ وَإِنْ كَانَ اَحَدُهُمَا قَدْ لَبْنَ فِي الْأَرْضِ أَوْ بَني أَوْ حَفَرَ فَهِيَ فِي يَدِهِ لِوُجُودِ التَّصَرُّفِ وَالْإِسْتِعْمَالِ فِيهَا
He said: And if two men claim a land, meaning each of them claims that it is in his hand (possession), it is not ruled that it is in the hand of one of them until they establish evidence that it is in their hands, because the hand (possession) in it is not witnessed due to the difficulty of bringing it, and what is absent from the knowledge of the judge, evidence establishes it. If one of them establishes evidence, it is placed in his hand because the proof is established, for possession is an intended right. If both establish evidence, it is placed in their hands for what we have explained. So it is not deserved for one of them without proof. And if one of them has placed bricks in the land, or built, or dug, then it is in his hand due to the existence of disposition and usage in it.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on claims deals with a situation where two men claim a piece of land, each asserting it is in his possession. The qadi does not rule for either until they provide evidence (bayyinah) that the land is in their possession, because possession is not visible and cannot be brought before the court. Whatever is absent from the judge's knowledge, evidence establishes it. If one provides evidence, the land is placed in his possession as proof is established. If both provide evidence, it is placed in both their possessions. However, if one has placed bricks, built, or dug a well on the land, then it is considered in his possession due to his disposition (tasarruf) and usage, indicating physical control.

Key Terms
البينة (al-bayyinah): Legal evidence, typically testimony of witnesses, required to prove possession when physical control is not observable.
اليد (al-yad): Hand; metaphor for possession or control over property.
التصرف (al-tasarruf): Disposition; physical acts like building or digging that indicate control and ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If one of the two claimants has built a structure on the disputed land, what is the ruling?
A) The land is divided equally between them
B) The land is given to the one who built due to his disposition
C) The land is left without judgment until both provide evidence
D) The builder is considered a trespasser

Key Takeaway
Possession of land is established by visible control, evidence (bayyinah), or physical acts of disposition like building or digging.
