ديعة
قسیم کی جائے ان سے تکلیف پر اس besturdubo
( بلکہ اس مقتضی کا ان دونوں کے ایک ساتھ قسم لینے سے بھی ہو جاتا ہے ) حالانکہ یہاں مقصود یہی ہے کہ
کے لئے علیحد ہ قسم کی جائے۔ والاظهر في تعليله ههنا ما ذكره صاحب الكافي حيث قال وانما يحلف لكل واحد منهما بانفراده لان كل واحد منهما ادعاه بانفراده قوله فينكشف وجه القضاء صاحب عنایہ نے وجہ قضاء کے بیان میں تین احتمال ذکر کرتے ہوئے کہا ہے بان يقضى بالالف للاول اولِلثانى او لهما جميعًا صاحب نتائج کہتے ہیں کہ اوللثانی والا احتمال غلط ہے۔ اس لئے کہ اوّل کے لئے قابض کے انکار قسم کے بعد ثانی کے لئے ایک ہزار کے حکیم ہونے کا کوئی سوال ہی نہیں ہے۔ پس یہاں دو ہی صورتوں کا احتمال ہے کہ قاضی ہزار کا فیصلہ دونوں کے لئے کرے یا صرف اول کے لئے یہ واضح ہو جائے اور تعجب یہ ہے کہ صاحب عنایہ نے تعلیل میں خود کہا ہے۔
لانه لو حلف للثانى فلاشئى له والا لف كله لِلأَوَّل ولونكل لِلثَّانِي ايضا كان الالف بينهما اس تعلیل سے یہ بات یقینی ہو جاتی ہے کہ یہاں صرف دو ہی احتمال ہیں۔ دراصل صاحب عنایہ کی لغزش کا منشاء۔ وجہ قضاء کے بیان میں شراح کا یہ قول ہے بان يقضى بالالف لهما اولاحدهما " کہ موصوف نے اولا حد ھما کو اول اور ثانی دونوں کے لئے عام سمجھ لیا حالانکہ احد هما سے ان کی مراد صرف مدعی اول ہے۔

قاضی نے پہلے والے کے لئے فیصلہ کیا جب قابض نے اول کے لئے قسم کھانے سے انکار
کیا تو دوسرے کے بارے میں امام بزودی کا نقطۂ نظر
وَلَوْ قَضَى الْقَاضِي لِلْأَوَّلِ حِيْنَ نَكَلَ ذَكَرَ الْإِمَامُ الْبَزْدَوِى فِي شَرْحِ الْجَامِعِ الصَّغِيْرِ أَنَّهُ يُحَلَّفُ لِلنَّانِي فَإِذَا نَكَلَ يُقْضَى بَيْنَهُمَا لاَنَّ الْقَضَاءَ لِلأَوَّلِ لَا يُبْطِلُ حَقُّ الثَّانِي لأَنَّهُ يُقَدِّمُهُ إِمَّا بِنَفْسِهِ أَوْ بِالْقُرْعَةِ وَكُلُّ ذَالِكَ لَا يُبْطِلُ حَقَّ الثَّانِي

ترجمہ اور اگر قاضی نے اول کے لئے حکم دیا جس وقت کہ قابض نے اول کے لئے قسم کھانے سے انکار کیا تو امام بزدوی نے شرح جامع صغیر میں ذکر کیا ہے کہ دوسرے کیلئے بھی قسم لی جائے گی اب اگر وہ انکار کرے تو موجودہ ہزار درہم دونوں میں مشترک ہونے کا حکم دیا جائے گا۔ اس لئے کہ اول کے لئے حکم دینا ثانی کا حق باطل نہیں کرتا۔ کیونکہ قاضی نے اس کو اپنے اختیار سے یا قرعہ سے اول بنادیا تھا اور ان میں سے کوئی ایک بات بھی ثانی کا حق باطل نہیں کرتی۔

تشريح ... قوله ولو قضى القاضی - اگر قابض نے مدعی اول کے لئے قسم کھانے سے انکار کیا اور قاضی نے اسی وقت اول کے لئے حکم کر دیا تو شیخ بزدوی نے شرح جامع میں ذکر کیا ہے کہ (قضاء نافذ نہ ہوگی پس ) مدعی ثانی کے لئے بھی قسم کی جائے گی۔ اگر اس نے اس سے انکار کیا تو موجودہ ہزار درہم کی نسبت ( جن کا حکم مدعی اول کے لئے کر دیا تھا) اب بدل کر یوں حکم دیا جائے گا کہ وہ دونوں میں مشترک ہیں۔ کیونکہ اول کے لئے حکم دے دینا دوسرے کا حق باطل نہیں کرتا اس لئے کہ قاضی نے اس کو اپنے اختیار سے اول بنایا تھایا قرعہ اندازی میں اس کا نام پہلے نکل آیا تھا۔ اور ان میں سے کوئی بات ایسی نہیں جو دوسرے کا حق مٹادے پھر اگر وہ ثانی کے لئے قسم کھالے تو شیخ بز دوئی نے اس کا حکم ذکر نہیں کیا۔ البتہ ان کے بھائی ابو اللیث نے کہا ہے فان حلف يقضى بنكوله لِلْأَوَّل ۔
Book of Deposit. So if the holder takes an oath for both, nothing will be for them because no proof is found. And if for the first [؟] the ruling will be given. Because proof... And if the first claimant refuses to take an oath, then a ruling will not be given immediately; rather, an oath will be taken for the second claimant. Contrary to this, if the defendant (the holder) confesses to one of the two claimants, a ruling will be given for the one confessed to, because confession is a proof that is self-operative. So with the confession, a ruling will be given immediately. As for refusal, it is not self-operative; rather, it becomes a proof only when the refusal occurs in the judge's court. Therefore, in the case of refusal, it is permissible to delay the first ruling so that he may take an oath for the second claimant and the method of judgment becomes clear, whether he will decide the thousand for the first claimant or for both of them. Because if the holder also refuses to take an oath for the second, then the thousand will be shared between them both. Hence, delay in judgment. And if the holder also refuses to take an oath for the second claimant, then the thousand will be ruled to be half and half between the two claimants (this is the case mentioned in the book) because in terms of proof, both claimants are equal. Just as if both claimants establish evidence, then this same ruling applies. Also, one thousand dirhams become obligatory on the holder, and they will also be half and half between the two claimants, because his not taking an oath is a confession to both claims. That is, he made a right obligatory upon himself either by way of payment (according to Imam Abu Hanifa) or by way of confession (according to the Sahibayn), and confession is a proof for the confessor's own self. So the right of each of the two claimants became one thousand each, even though he only gave one thousand. So he has paid half of each one's right by means of the other's half right. So he becomes a guarantor for half of each of their rights. This is the ruling according to our scholars. Faqih Abu Layth said in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir that according to Ibn Abi Layla's view, only one thousand would be obligatory on the mentioned holder. His statement: 'Each one's claim is valid...' In Kifayah Sharh Taj al-Shari'ah and Nata'ij al-Afkar, it is said that by validity of the claim is meant validity individually, not collectively. Therefore, the author of al-Hidayah's reasoning 'because it is not necessary that they are truthful' is complete without complication. Sa'di Chalisi interpreted validity of the claims as being valid collectively and strained in explaining the text, saying that both claims are valid collectively, such that one claimant gave a thousand dirhams as a deposit to someone, then the depositee bought some goods from another and deposited that thousand dirhams with him. But according to the author of Nata'ij, this explanation is wrong because in the original issue it is stated that 'two men claimed, each of them that it is his deposit' which indicates that each of them claimed that he is the owner of the thousand and he deposited them. And it is obvious that a single specific thing being wholly owned by two persons simultaneously, and being deposited from both sides, is inconceivable. In the mentioned explanation, the ownership of the holder over the thousand dirhams from one of them had ceased due to the purchase of goods. So how can it be likely that he is truthful in both claims? His statement: 'Because of the difference of rights.' The author of 'Inayah and the author of Binayah and a group of commentators said in the reasoning for the difference of rights: 'because each of them claims a thousand.' But this reasoning is objected to: each claimant is not an absolute claimant of a thousand; rather, he claims the specific thousand dirhams that are in the possession of the defendant, as clarified in the formulation of the issue. And in the chapter on deposits, currency becomes specific, as is established in its place. And 'Allamah Zayla'i has clarified this in Tabyin, where he said: 'Because currency becomes specific in deposits and usurped property.' So the mentioned reasoning does not indicate a difference of rights. Sa'di Chalisi explained the difference of rights on another basis, and that is that the difference of right is due to the difference of the entitled person, because for each claimant there is a right to an oath due to the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him). The author of Nata'ij says that this explanation is useless here because each of them having a right to an oath... Ashraf al-Hidayah, volume eleven. Deposit. They will be divided, with difficulty upon it [?]. (Rather, this requirement is also fulfilled by taking oath from both of them together.) While here the intention is that an oath should be taken for each separately. And the clearest in its reasoning here is what the author of al-Kafi mentioned, who said: 'He swears for each of them separately because each of them claimed separately.' His statement: 'So the method of judgment becomes clear.' The author of 'Inayah, while mentioning three possibilities in explaining the method of judgment, said: 'That judgment be given for the thousand to the first, or to the second, or to both of them.' The author of Nata'ij says that the possibility of the second is wrong because after the holder's refusal of oath for the first, there is no question of judging the thousand for the second. So here only two possibilities exist: either the judge decides the thousand for both, or it becomes clear that it is only for the first. And it is surprising that the author of 'Inayah himself said in his reasoning: 'Because if he swears for the second, there is nothing for him, and if he swears for the first, the whole thousand is for him. And if he also refuses for the second, the thousand is between them.' This reasoning makes it certain that only two possibilities exist here. Actually, the source of the author of 'Inayah's slip is the statement of the commentators in explaining the method of judgment: 'that judgment be given for the thousand to both of them or to one of them.' He understood 'one of them' as general for both first and second, while by 'one of them' they meant only the first claimant. And if the judge gave judgment for the first when the holder refused to take an oath for the first, then Imam Bazdawi's viewpoint regarding the second: 'And if the judge gave judgment for the first when he refused, Imam al-Bazdawi mentioned in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir that an oath will be taken for the second, and if he refuses, judgment will be given between them, because the judgment for the first does not nullify the right of the second, since he gave him priority either by his own choice or by lot, and none of that nullifies the right of the second.' Translation: And if the judge gave judgment for the first when the holder refused to take an oath for the first, Imam Bazdawi mentioned in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir that an oath will also be taken for the second. Now if he refuses, then the existing thousand dirhams will be ruled to be shared between both. Because giving judgment for the first does not invalidate the right of the second, since the judge made him first by his own choice or by lot, and none of these matters invalidate the right of the second. Elucidation: His statement: 'And if the judge gave judgment...' - If the holder refused to take an oath for the first claimant and the judge immediately gave judgment for the first, then Shaykh Bazdawi mentioned in Sharh al-Jami' that (the judgment will not be effective), so an oath will also be taken for the second claimant. If he refuses, then regarding the existing thousand dirhams (which had been judged for the first claimant) the ruling will now be changed such that they are shared between both. Because giving judgment for the first does not nullify the right of the second, since the judge made him first by his own choice or his name came out first in the lottery. And none of these things erase the right of the second. Then if he (the second) takes an oath, Shaykh Bazdawi did not mention its ruling. However, his brother Abu al-Layth said: 'If he swears, judgment will be given based on his refusal (of the first) for the first.'
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on a ruling from a Hanafi fiqh text (likely al-Hidayah) concerning a dispute where two individuals each claim that a specific thousand dirhams held by a depositee (qabid) were deposited by them. The passage covers multiple scenarios and intra-Hanafi disagreements.

The core ruling: If the depositee (qabid) swears an oath for both claimants that he does not owe them, then neither claimant gets anything because no proof is established. If he refuses to swear for the first claimant (nukul), the judge does not immediately rule for the first; instead, he takes an oath from the second claimant. If the qabid also refuses for the second, then the thousand is divided equally between the two claimants. This is because both claimants are equal in terms of proof (both have the same legal status).

An important nuance: If the qabid confesses (iqrar) to one of the claimants, judgment is given immediately for that claimant because confession is a self-operative proof. Refusal (nukul) is not self-operative; it becomes a proof only when it occurs in the judge's court. Hence, the judge delays ruling for the first to see if the second also refuses.

The passage then discusses the liability of the qabid. By refusing to swear for both, he is deemed to have admitted both claims. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, this is like a payment (badl) that creates liability, while according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is like a confession (iqrar). In either case, he becomes liable for one thousand dirhams to be shared between the two claimants. However, since he only has one thousand (the actual deposit), he pays half to each, and the other half is offset because each half pays for the other. This is the Hanafi position. Ibn Abi Layla differed, holding that only one thousand is due (to be divided).

Next, the commentary explains the phrase 'each claimant's claim is valid'. It clarifies that validity means individually, not collectively. A collective validity is impossible because one specific item cannot be owned by two persons simultaneously. The attempt by Sa'di Chalisi to interpret it collectively is rejected.

Then it discusses the reasoning for the difference of rights (taghayur al-haqqain). Some commentators said it is because each claims a thousand, but this is objected to because each claims a specific identified thousand in the qabid's possession, and currency becomes specific in deposits. The correct reasoning is that the difference is due to the difference of the entitled persons: each has the right to an oath. The author of al-Kafi gives the best reasoning: each is sworn separately because each claimed separately.

Finally, the passage discusses the scenario where the judge prematurely rules for the first claimant before taking an oath from the second. According to Imam Bazdawi, such a judgment is not effective; the second claimant must still be given an oath, and if he refuses, the thousand is shared. This is because the judge's prioritization (whether by choice or lot) does not nullify the second's right. If the second swears, Abu al-Layth says the judgment reverts to the first based on the first's refusal.

Throughout, the commentary emphasizes the procedural fairness in a complex dispute where two claimants have equal standing, and the depositee's refusal to swear is treated as an admission creating joint liability.

Key Terms
وديعة (wadi'ah): A deposit; a contract where one entrusts property to another for safekeeping without compensation.
نكول (nukul): Refusal of the defendant to take an oath after it is offered, which is treated as an admission of the claim.
اقرار (iqrar): Confession or admission of a right against oneself, which is a binding proof.
يمين (yamin): Oath; a sworn statement taken from a party to establish or refute a claim.
مدعى (mudda'i): Claimant; a person who asserts a right against another.
قابض (qabid): Holder; the person in physical possession of the deposit (the depositee).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of two claimants to a deposit, what should the judge do if the depositee (qabid) refuses to take an oath for the first claimant?
A) Immediately rule in favor of the first claimant.
B) Take an oath from the second claimant before making a decision.
C) Dismiss the first claimant's case.
D) Order the depositee to pay both claimants.

Key Takeaway
A depositee's refusal to swear (nukul) does not immediately entitle the first claimant; the judge must delay to hear the second claimant, unlike confession which is self-operative.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
8 min
Liability of the Depositee After Refusing Oaths for Both Claimants
Commentary on the liability of the depositee after nukul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the depositee becomes liable for one thousand dirhams divided equally when he refuses oaths for both claimants, and articulate the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding the legal nature of nukul (badl vs iqrar).

Core Idea
Refusal to swear for both claimants creates liability for the full deposit divided equally, with an offset mechanism.

In the previous lesson, we saw that if the depositee refuses to swear for both claimants, the thousand dirhams are divided equally. This lesson dives deeper into the legal basis for this ruling: why nukul creates liability, the difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on whether it is payment (badl) or confession (iqrar), and the offset that makes the depositee a guarantor for half of each claimant's right.

Guided Path
1
Understand the consequence of dual nukul
When the depositee refuses to swear for both claimants, the thousand dirhams are ruled to be shared half and half. This is because both claimants are equal in proof.
This is analogous to when both claimants present evidence (bayyinah).
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the nature of nukul
Imam Abu Hanifa views nukul as 'badl' (payment), while the Sahibayn view it as 'iqrar' (confession). Both lead to the same practical result: liability.
The text says: 'either by way of payment (Abu Hanifa) or by way of confession (Sahibayn)'.
3
Analyze the offset mechanism
The depositee owes each claimant a thousand, but because he only has one thousand, he pays half to each. The other half is offset: each half pays for the other, making him a guarantor for the other half.
This ensures justice: the depositee does not lose more than the actual deposit.
4
Contrast with the view of Ibn Abi Layla
Ibn Abi Layla holds that only one thousand is due (to be divided). The Hanafis argue that nukul on both claims creates a theoretical double liability, but the offset prevents double payment.
The passage cites Faqih Abu Layth reporting this difference.

نیز قابض الف پر ایک ہزار درہم اور واجب ہوں گے اور وہ بھی دونوں مدعیوں میں نصفا نصف ہوں گے اس لئے کہ اس کا قسم نہ کھانا دونوں دعووں کا اقرار ہوا یعنی اس نے بطریق بذل ( امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک) یا بطریق اقرار ( صاحبین کے نزدیک ) اپنے اوپر حق واجب کر لیا اور اقرار خود مقر کی ذات کے لئے حجت ہوتا ہے۔ پس دونوں مدعیوں کا حق ایک ایک ہزار ہوا۔ حالانکہ اس نے صرف ایک ہزار دیا ہے۔ تو وہ ہر ایک کا نصف حق دوسرے کے نصف حق کے ذریعہ سے ادا کرنے والا ہوا۔ پس وہ دونوں کے نصف نصف حق کا اور ضامن ہو گا۔ یہ حکم ہمارے علماء کے یہاں ہے فقیہ ابولیث نے شرح جامع صغیر میں کہا ہے کہ ابن ابی لیلیٰ کے قول میں قابض مذکور پر صرف ایک ہزار ہی واجب ہوں گے۔

قوله دعوى كل واحد صحيحة... کفایہ شرح تاج الشریعہ اور نتائج الافکار میں ہے کہ صحت دعوی سے مراد بطریق انفرا صحیح ہونا ہے نہ کہ بطریق اجتماع لہذا صاحب ہدایہ کی تعلیل " لا حتما لها الصدق " بلا کلفت تام ہے۔ سعدی چلسی نے صحت دعوئی کو بطریق اجتماع صحیح ہونے پر محمول کر کے تو جیہ مقام میں بھینچ تان کی ہے اور کہا ہے کہ اجتماعی طور پر ان دونوں کا دعوی صحیح ہے۔ بایں طور کہ ایک مدعی نے کسی کو ہزار درہم ودیعت دیئے۔ مودع نے دوسرے سے کوئی اسباب خرید کر وہ ہزار درہم اسی کے پاس ودیعت رکھ دیئے۔ لیکن بقول صاحب نتائج یہ توجیہ غلط ہے اس لئے کہ اصل مسئلہ میں جو یہ مذکور ہے فادعا ها رجلان كل واحد منهما انهاله اودعها اياه " یا اس پر دال ہے کہ ان میں سے ہر ایک نے یہ دعوی کیا ہے کہ فی الحال ہزار کا مالک وہی ہے اور اسی نے ودیعت رکھے ہیں اور یہ ظاہر ہے کہ عین واحد کا بحالت واحدہ پورے طور پر دو شخصوں کی ملک ہونا اسی طرح دو کی طرف سے مودع ہونا غیر متصور ہے اور توجیہ مذکور میں قابض کے پاس ان میں سے ایک کا ہزار درہم ودیعت رکھنا او ان کا مالک ہونا خرید اسباب کی وجہ سے زائل ہو چکا۔ فکیف یحتمل ان يصد قامعا دعواهما.

قاضی نے پہلے والے کے لئے فیصلہ کیا جب قابض نے اول کے لئے قسم کھانے سے انکار

وَلَوْ قَضَى الْقَاضِي لِلْأَوَّلِ حِيْنَ نَكَلَ ذَكَرَ الْإِمَامُ الْبَزْدَوِى فِي شَرْحِ الْجَامِعِ الصَّغِيْرِ أَنَّهُ يُحَلَّفُ لِلنَّانِي فَإِذَا نَكَلَ يُقْضَى بَيْنَهُمَا لاَنَّ الْقَضَاءَ لِلأَوَّلِ لَا يُبْطِلُ حَقُّ الثَّانِي لأَنَّهُ يُقَدِّمُهُ إِمَّا بِنَفْسِهِ أَوْ بِالْقُرْعَةِ وَكُلُّ ذَالِكَ لَا يُبْطِلُ حَقَّ الثَّانِي

ترجمہ اور اگر قاضی نے اول کے لئے حکم دیا جس وقت کہ قابض نے اول کے لئے قسم کھانے سے انکار کیا تو امام بزدوی نے شرح جامع صغیر میں ذکر کیا ہے کہ دوسرے کیلئے بھی قسم لی جائے گی اب اگر وہ انکار کرے تو موجودہ ہزار درہم دونوں میں مشترک ہونے کا حکم دیا جائے گا۔ اس لئے کہ اول کے لئے حکم دینا ثانی کا حق باطل نہیں کرتا۔ کیونکہ قاضی نے اس کو اپنے اختیار سے یا قرعہ سے اول بنادیا تھا اور ان میں سے کوئی ایک بات بھی ثانی کا حق باطل نہیں کرتی۔

تشريح ... قوله ولو قضى القاضی - اگر قابض نے مدعی اول کے لئے قسم کھانے سے انکار کیا اور قاضی نے اسی وقت اول کے لئے حکم کر دیا تو شیخ بزدوی نے شرح جامع میں ذکر کیا ہے کہ (قضاء نافذ نہ ہوگی پس ) مدعی ثانی کے لئے بھی قسم کی جائے گی۔ اگر اس نے اس سے انکار کیا تو موجودہ ہزار درہم کی نسبت ( جن کا حکم مدعی اول کے لئے کر دیا تھا) اب بدل کر یوں حکم دیا جائے گا کہ وہ دونوں میں مشترک ہیں۔ کیونکہ اول کے لئے حکم دے دینا دوسرے کا حق باطل نہیں کرتا اس لئے کہ قاضی نے اس کو اپنے اختیار سے اول بنایا تھایا قرعہ اندازی میں اس کا نام پہلے نکل آیا تھا۔ اور ان میں سے کوئی بات ایسی نہیں جو دوسرے کا حق مٹادے پھر اگر وہ ثانی کے لئے قسم کھالے تو شیخ بز دوئی نے اس کا حکم ذکر نہیں کیا۔ البتہ ان کے بھائی ابو اللیث نے کہا ہے فان حلف يقضى بنكوله لِلْأَوَّل ۔
Book of Deposit. So if the holder takes an oath for both, nothing will be for them because no proof is found. And if for the first [؟] the ruling will be given. Because proof... And if the first claimant refuses to take an oath, then a ruling will not be given immediately; rather, an oath will be taken for the second claimant. Contrary to this, if the defendant (the holder) confesses to one of the two claimants, a ruling will be given for the one confessed to, because confession is a proof that is self-operative. So with the confession, a ruling will be given immediately. As for refusal, it is not self-operative; rather, it becomes a proof only when the refusal occurs in the judge's court. Therefore, in the case of refusal, it is permissible to delay the first ruling so that he may take an oath for the second claimant and the method of judgment becomes clear, whether he will decide the thousand for the first claimant or for both of them. Because if the holder also refuses to take an oath for the second, then the thousand will be shared between them both. Hence, delay in judgment. And if the holder also refuses to take an oath for the second claimant, then the thousand will be ruled to be half and half between the two claimants (this is the case mentioned in the book) because in terms of proof, both claimants are equal. Just as if both claimants establish evidence, then this same ruling applies. Also, one thousand dirhams become obligatory on the holder, and they will also be half and half between the two claimants, because his not taking an oath is a confession to both claims. That is, he made a right obligatory upon himself either by way of payment (according to Imam Abu Hanifa) or by way of confession (according to the Sahibayn), and confession is a proof for the confessor's own self. So the right of each of the two claimants became one thousand each, even though he only gave one thousand. So he has paid half of each one's right by means of the other's half right. So he becomes a guarantor for half of each of their rights. This is the ruling according to our scholars. Faqih Abu Layth said in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir that according to Ibn Abi Layla's view, only one thousand would be obligatory on the mentioned holder. His statement: 'Each one's claim is valid...' In Kifayah Sharh Taj al-Shari'ah and Nata'ij al-Afkar, it is said that by validity of the claim is meant validity individually, not collectively. Therefore, the author of al-Hidayah's reasoning 'because it is not necessary that they are truthful' is complete without complication. Sa'di Chalisi interpreted validity of the claims as being valid collectively and strained in explaining the text, saying that both claims are valid collectively, such that one claimant gave a thousand dirhams as a deposit to someone, then the depositee bought some goods from another and deposited that thousand dirhams with him. But according to the author of Nata'ij, this explanation is wrong because in the original issue it is stated that 'two men claimed, each of them that it is his deposit' which indicates that each of them claimed that he is the owner of the thousand and he deposited them. And it is obvious that a single specific thing being wholly owned by two persons simultaneously, and being deposited from both sides, is inconceivable. In the mentioned explanation, the ownership of the holder over the thousand dirhams from one of them had ceased due to the purchase of goods. So how can it be likely that he is truthful in both claims? His statement: 'Because of the difference of rights.' The author of 'Inayah and the author of Binayah and a group of commentators said in the reasoning for the difference of rights: 'because each of them claims a thousand.' But this reasoning is objected to: each claimant is not an absolute claimant of a thousand; rather, he claims the specific thousand dirhams that are in the possession of the defendant, as clarified in the formulation of the issue. And in the chapter on deposits, currency becomes specific, as is established in its place. And 'Allamah Zayla'i has clarified this in Tabyin, where he said: 'Because currency becomes specific in deposits and usurped property.' So the mentioned reasoning does not indicate a difference of rights. Sa'di Chalisi explained the difference of rights on another basis, and that is that the difference of right is due to the difference of the entitled person, because for each claimant there is a right to an oath due to the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him). The author of Nata'ij says that this explanation is useless here because each of them having a right to an oath... Ashraf al-Hidayah, volume eleven. Deposit. They will be divided, with difficulty upon it [?]. (Rather, this requirement is also fulfilled by taking oath from both of them together.) While here the intention is that an oath should be taken for each separately. And the clearest in its reasoning here is what the author of al-Kafi mentioned, who said: 'He swears for each of them separately because each of them claimed separately.' His statement: 'So the method of judgment becomes clear.' The author of 'Inayah, while mentioning three possibilities in explaining the method of judgment, said: 'That judgment be given for the thousand to the first, or to the second, or to both of them.' The author of Nata'ij says that the possibility of the second is wrong because after the holder's refusal of oath for the first, there is no question of judging the thousand for the second. So here only two possibilities exist: either the judge decides the thousand for both, or it becomes clear that it is only for the first. And it is surprising that the author of 'Inayah himself said in his reasoning: 'Because if he swears for the second, there is nothing for him, and if he swears for the first, the whole thousand is for him. And if he also refuses for the second, the thousand is between them.' This reasoning makes it certain that only two possibilities exist here. Actually, the source of the author of 'Inayah's slip is the statement of the commentators in explaining the method of judgment: 'that judgment be given for the thousand to both of them or to one of them.' He understood 'one of them' as general for both first and second, while by 'one of them' they meant only the first claimant. And if the judge gave judgment for the first when the holder refused to take an oath for the first, then Imam Bazdawi's viewpoint regarding the second: 'And if the judge gave judgment for the first when he refused, Imam al-Bazdawi mentioned in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir that an oath will be taken for the second, and if he refuses, judgment will be given between them, because the judgment for the first does not nullify the right of the second, since he gave him priority either by his own choice or by lot, and none of that nullifies the right of the second.' Translation: And if the judge gave judgment for the first when the holder refused to take an oath for the first, Imam Bazdawi mentioned in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir that an oath will also be taken for the second. Now if he refuses, then the existing thousand dirhams will be ruled to be shared between both. Because giving judgment for the first does not invalidate the right of the second, since the judge made him first by his own choice or by lot, and none of these matters invalidate the right of the second. Elucidation: His statement: 'And if the judge gave judgment...' - If the holder refused to take an oath for the first claimant and the judge immediately gave judgment for the first, then Shaykh Bazdawi mentioned in Sharh al-Jami' that (the judgment will not be effective), so an oath will also be taken for the second claimant. If he refuses, then regarding the existing thousand dirhams (which had been judged for the first claimant) the ruling will now be changed such that they are shared between both. Because giving judgment for the first does not nullify the right of the second, since the judge made him first by his own choice or his name came out first in the lottery. And none of these things erase the right of the second. Then if he (the second) takes an oath, Shaykh Bazdawi did not mention its ruling. However, his brother Abu al-Layth said: 'If he swears, judgment will be given based on his refusal (of the first) for the first.'
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on a ruling from a Hanafi fiqh text (likely al-Hidayah) concerning a dispute where two individuals each claim that a specific thousand dirhams held by a depositee (qabid) were deposited by them. The passage covers multiple scenarios and intra-Hanafi disagreements.

The core ruling: If the depositee (qabid) swears an oath for both claimants that he does not owe them, then neither claimant gets anything because no proof is established. If he refuses to swear for the first claimant (nukul), the judge does not immediately rule for the first; instead, he takes an oath from the second claimant. If the qabid also refuses for the second, then the thousand is divided equally between the two claimants. This is because both claimants are equal in terms of proof (both have the same legal status).

An important nuance: If the qabid confesses (iqrar) to one of the claimants, judgment is given immediately for that claimant because confession is a self-operative proof. Refusal (nukul) is not self-operative; it becomes a proof only when it occurs in the judge's court. Hence, the judge delays ruling for the first to see if the second also refuses.

The passage then discusses the liability of the qabid. By refusing to swear for both, he is deemed to have admitted both claims. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, this is like a payment (badl) that creates liability, while according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is like a confession (iqrar). In either case, he becomes liable for one thousand dirhams to be shared between the two claimants. However, since he only has one thousand (the actual deposit), he pays half to each, and the other half is offset because each half pays for the other. This is the Hanafi position. Ibn Abi Layla differed, holding that only one thousand is due (to be divided).

Next, the commentary explains the phrase 'each claimant's claim is valid'. It clarifies that validity means individually, not collectively. A collective validity is impossible because one specific item cannot be owned by two persons simultaneously. The attempt by Sa'di Chalisi to interpret it collectively is rejected.

Then it discusses the reasoning for the difference of rights (taghayur al-haqqain). Some commentators said it is because each claims a thousand, but this is objected to because each claims a specific identified thousand in the qabid's possession, and currency becomes specific in deposits. The correct reasoning is that the difference is due to the difference of the entitled persons: each has the right to an oath. The author of al-Kafi gives the best reasoning: each is sworn separately because each claimed separately.

Finally, the passage discusses the scenario where the judge prematurely rules for the first claimant before taking an oath from the second. According to Imam Bazdawi, such a judgment is not effective; the second claimant must still be given an oath, and if he refuses, the thousand is shared. This is because the judge's prioritization (whether by choice or lot) does not nullify the second's right. If the second swears, Abu al-Layth says the judgment reverts to the first based on the first's refusal.

Throughout, the commentary emphasizes the procedural fairness in a complex dispute where two claimants have equal standing, and the depositee's refusal to swear is treated as an admission creating joint liability.

Key Terms
بذل (badl): Payment or exchange; Imam Abu Hanifa's view that nukul is like a payment that creates liability.
ضامن (damin): Guarantor; one who is responsible for a debt.
تقابل (taqabul): Offset or set-off; the mechanism by which two debts cancel each other partially.
ابن ابی لیلی (Ibn Abi Layla): A prominent early Hanafi jurist who differed on this ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the practical outcome when a depositee refuses to swear for both claimants?
A) The depositee pays 2000 dirhams to the claimants.
B) The depositee pays 1000 dirhams divided equally between the two claimants.
C) The depositee is not liable because he refused the oath.
D) The depositee chooses which claimant to pay.

Key Takeaway
Dual nukul makes the depositee liable for the deposit divided equally, with an offset mechanism that prevents double payment while acknowledging both claims.

The Validity of Each Claim Individually and the Difference of Rights
Commentary on the validity of each claim and the reasoning for difference of rights

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the claims of two depositors are valid individually but not collectively, and analyze the different rationales for 'difference of rights' (taghayur al-haqqain) offered by Hanafi commentators.

Core Idea
Each claim is valid individually because the claimants are separate persons, but collectively they cannot both own the same specific property simultaneously.

In the earlier scenario, both claimants are treated equally, but how can that be if only one of them truly owns the deposit? This passage clarifies that the validity of each claim is considered individually, not collectively. It then discusses the reasoning for 'difference of rights' (taghayur al-haqqain), with commentators offering various explanations. We will examine the objections and the preferred reasoning from al-Kafi.

Guided Path
1
Understand the premise: each claim is valid individually
The text states that 'each claimant's claim is valid' means valid when considered alone, not collectively. It is possible for two people to each plausibly claim the same property, but they cannot both be true owners.
This is a legal fiction for the sake of procedure; the judge treats them equally in terms of proof.
2
Reject the interpretation of collective validity
Sa'di Chalisi attempted to interpret the claims as collectively valid by imagining a scenario where one person's deposit becomes another's due to a purchase. The author of Nata'ij rejects this as inconsistent with the original problem.
The original problem states each claims the deposit is his own; collective ownership of a specific item is impossible.
3
Examine the different rationales for 'difference of rights'
Some commentators said the difference is because each claims a thousand (different amounts? not exactly). Others said the difference arises from the difference of the persons entitled (each has a right to an oath).
The first reasoning is objected to because both claimants claim the same specific thousand.
4
Identify the preferred reasoning from al-Kafi
The author of al-Kafi states that the judge swears each claimant separately because each claimed separately. This is the clearest reasoning according to the passage.
This focuses on the procedural aspect: the oath is individual because the claim is individual.

پس اگر قابض دونوں کے لئے قسم کھالے تو ان کے لئے کچھ نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ حجت نہیں پائی گئی۔ اور اگر اول کے لئے [؟] سے کا حکم لئے دے دیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ حجبت ( اور مدعی اول قسم کھانے سے انکار کیا تو ابھی حکم نہیں دیا جائے گا بلکہ دوسرے مدعی کے لئے قسم لی جائے گی اس کے برخلاف اگر مدعی علیہ ( قابض ) نے دونوں مدعیوں میں سے کسی ایک کے لئے اقرار کر لیا تو مقرلہ کے لئے حکم کر دیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اقرار ایک ایسی حجت ہے جو بذات خود موجب ہے تو اقرار کے ساتھ ہی حکم کر دیا جائے گا۔ رہا تم سے انکار کرنا سو یہ بذات خود موجب نہیں بلکہ یہ محبت اسی وقت ہوتا ہے جب قاضی کی مجلس میں انکار کرے۔ لہذا بصورت انکار حکم اول میں تاخیر کرنا جائز ہوگا۔ تاکہ دوسرے مدعی کے لئے قسم لے اور حکیم قضاء کا طریقہ منکشف ہو جائے کہ وہ ہزار کا فیصلہ مدعی اول کے لئے یا ان دونوں کے لئے کرے اس واسطے کہ قابض اگر ثانی کے لئے بھی قسم کھانے سے انکار کرتا ہے تو ہزار دونوں میں مشترک ہوں گے فلذا توقف في القضاء اور اگر قابض نے دوسرے مدعی کے لئے بھی قسم کھانے بھی انکار کر دیا تو ہزار دور ہم ان دونوں مدعیوں کے درمیان نصفا نصف ہونے کا حکم دیا جائے گا ( کتاب میں یہی صورت مذکور ہے ) کیونکہ حجت میں وہ دونوں مدعی برابر ہیں۔ جیسے اگر وہ دونوں مدعی پینہ قائم کر دیں۔ تب بھی یہی حکم ہوتا ہے۔

نیز قابض الف پر ایک ہزار درہم اور واجب ہوں گے اور وہ بھی دونوں مدعیوں میں نصفا نصف ہوں گے اس لئے کہ اس کا قسم نہ کھانا دونوں دعووں کا اقرار ہوا یعنی اس نے بطریق بذل ( امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک) یا بطریق اقرار ( صاحبین کے نزدیک ) اپنے اوپر حق واجب کر لیا اور اقرار خود مقر کی ذات کے لئے حجت ہوتا ہے۔ پس دونوں مدعیوں کا حق ایک ایک ہزار ہوا۔ حالانکہ اس نے صرف ایک ہزار دیا ہے۔ تو وہ ہر ایک کا نصف حق دوسرے کے نصف حق کے ذریعہ سے ادا کرنے والا ہوا۔ پس وہ دونوں کے نصف نصف حق کا اور ضامن ہو گا۔ یہ حکم ہمارے علماء کے یہاں ہے فقیہ ابولیث نے شرح جامع صغیر میں کہا ہے کہ ابن ابی لیلیٰ کے قول میں قابض مذکور پر صرف ایک ہزار ہی واجب ہوں گے۔

قوله دعوى كل واحد صحيحة... کفایہ شرح تاج الشریعہ اور نتائج الافکار میں ہے کہ صحت دعوی سے مراد بطریق انفرا صحیح ہونا ہے نہ کہ بطریق اجتماع لہذا صاحب ہدایہ کی تعلیل " لا حتما لها الصدق " بلا کلفت تام ہے۔ سعدی چلسی نے صحت دعوئی کو بطریق اجتماع صحیح ہونے پر محمول کر کے تو جیہ مقام میں بھینچ تان کی ہے اور کہا ہے کہ اجتماعی طور پر ان دونوں کا دعوی صحیح ہے۔ بایں طور کہ ایک مدعی نے کسی کو ہزار درہم ودیعت دیئے۔ مودع نے دوسرے سے کوئی اسباب خرید کر وہ ہزار درہم اسی کے پاس ودیعت رکھ دیئے۔ لیکن بقول صاحب نتائج یہ توجیہ غلط ہے اس لئے کہ اصل مسئلہ میں جو یہ مذکور ہے فادعا ها رجلان كل واحد منهما انهاله اودعها اياه " یا اس پر دال ہے کہ ان میں سے ہر ایک نے یہ دعوی کیا ہے کہ فی الحال ہزار کا مالک وہی ہے اور اسی نے ودیعت رکھے ہیں اور یہ ظاہر ہے کہ عین واحد کا بحالت واحدہ پورے طور پر دو شخصوں کی ملک ہونا اسی طرح دو کی طرف سے مودع ہونا غیر متصور ہے اور توجیہ مذکور میں قابض کے پاس ان میں سے ایک کا ہزار درہم ودیعت رکھنا او ان کا مالک ہونا خرید اسباب کی وجہ سے زائل ہو چکا۔ فکیف یحتمل ان يصد قامعا دعواهما.

قوله لتغاير الحقين صاحب عنایہ اور صاحب بنایہ وغیرہ شراح کی ایک جماعت نے تغایر حقین کی تعلیل میں کہا ہے لان کل واحد منھما یدگی الفا لیکن اس تعلیل پر یہ اعتراض ہوتا ہے کہ ان میں سے ہر ایک مدعی مطلق ہزار کا دعوی دار نہیں ہے بلکہ ان معین ہزار دراہم کا مدعی ہے جو مدعی علیہ کے قبضہ میں ہے۔ جیسا کہ وضع مسئلہ میں اس کی تصریح کی گئی ہے اور باب ودائع میں نقود متعین ہو جاتے ہیں۔ جیسا کہ اپنی جگہ ثابت ہے اور علامہ زیلعی نے تنہین میں اس کی تصریح کی ہے۔ حیث قال لأنَّ النقود تتعين في الودائع والمغضوب پس تعلیل مذکور تغایر حقین پر دال نہیں ہے۔ سعدی چلی نے تغایر حقین کی توجیہ ایک دوسرے نہج پر کی ہے اور وہ کہ کہ تغایر حق تغایر مستحق کی وجہ سے ہے کہ ان میں سے مدعی کے لئے حق یمین ہے۔ لقوله علیه السلام، صاحب نتائج کہتے ہیں کہ یہاں یہ توجیہ بے سود ہے اس لئے کہ ان میں سے ہر ایک کے لئے حق یمین ہونے کا

قسیم کی جائے ان سے تکلیف پر اس besturdubo
( بلکہ اس مقتضی کا ان دونوں کے ایک ساتھ قسم لینے سے بھی ہو جاتا ہے ) حالانکہ یہاں مقصود یہی ہے کہ
کے لئے علیحد ہ قسم کی جائے۔ والاظهر في تعليله ههنا ما ذكره صاحب الكافي حيث قال وانما يحلف لكل واحد منهما بانفراده لان كل واحد منهما ادعاه بانفراده قوله فينكشف وجه القضاء صاحب عنایہ نے وجہ قضاء کے بیان میں تین احتمال ذکر کرتے ہوئے کہا ہے بان يقضى بالالف للاول اولِلثانى او لهما جميعًا صاحب نتائج کہتے ہیں کہ اوللثانی والا احتمال غلط ہے۔ اس لئے کہ اوّل کے لئے قابض کے انکار قسم کے بعد ثانی کے لئے ایک ہزار کے حکیم ہونے کا کوئی سوال ہی نہیں ہے۔ پس یہاں دو ہی صورتوں کا احتمال ہے کہ قاضی ہزار کا فیصلہ دونوں کے لئے کرے یا صرف اول کے لئے یہ واضح ہو جائے اور تعجب یہ ہے کہ صاحب عنایہ نے تعلیل میں خود کہا ہے۔
لانه لو حلف للثانى فلاشئى له والا لف كله لِلأَوَّل ولونكل لِلثَّانِي ايضا كان الالف بينهما اس تعلیل سے یہ بات یقینی ہو جاتی ہے کہ یہاں صرف دو ہی احتمال ہیں۔ دراصل صاحب عنایہ کی لغزش کا منشاء۔ وجہ قضاء کے بیان میں شراح کا یہ قول ہے بان يقضى بالالف لهما اولاحدهما " کہ موصوف نے اولا حد ھما کو اول اور ثانی دونوں کے لئے عام سمجھ لیا حالانکہ احد هما سے ان کی مراد صرف مدعی اول ہے۔

قاضی نے پہلے والے کے لئے فیصلہ کیا جب قابض نے اول کے لئے قسم کھانے سے انکار
کیا تو دوسرے کے بارے میں امام بزودی کا نقطۂ نظر
وَلَوْ قَضَى الْقَاضِي لِلْأَوَّلِ حِيْنَ نَكَلَ ذَكَرَ الْإِمَامُ الْبَزْدَوِى فِي شَرْحِ الْجَامِعِ الصَّغِيْرِ أَنَّهُ يُحَلَّفُ لِلنَّانِي فَإِذَا نَكَلَ يُقْضَى بَيْنَهُمَا لاَنَّ الْقَضَاءَ لِلأَوَّلِ لَا يُبْطِلُ حَقُّ الثَّانِي لأَنَّهُ يُقَدِّمُهُ إِمَّا بِنَفْسِهِ أَوْ بِالْقُرْعَةِ وَكُلُّ ذَالِكَ لَا يُبْطِلُ حَقَّ الثَّانِي

ترجمہ اور اگر قاضی نے اول کے لئے حکم دیا جس وقت کہ قابض نے اول کے لئے قسم کھانے سے انکار کیا تو امام بزدوی نے شرح جامع صغیر میں ذکر کیا ہے کہ دوسرے کیلئے بھی قسم لی جائے گی اب اگر وہ انکار کرے تو موجودہ ہزار درہم دونوں میں مشترک ہونے کا حکم دیا جائے گا۔ اس لئے کہ اول کے لئے حکم دینا ثانی کا حق باطل نہیں کرتا۔ کیونکہ قاضی نے اس کو اپنے اختیار سے یا قرعہ سے اول بنادیا تھا اور ان میں سے کوئی ایک بات بھی ثانی کا حق باطل نہیں کرتی۔

تشريح ... قوله ولو قضى القاضی - اگر قابض نے مدعی اول کے لئے قسم کھانے سے انکار کیا اور قاضی نے اسی وقت اول کے لئے حکم کر دیا تو شیخ بزدوی نے شرح جامع میں ذکر کیا ہے کہ (قضاء نافذ نہ ہوگی پس ) مدعی ثانی کے لئے بھی قسم کی جائے گی۔ اگر اس نے اس سے انکار کیا تو موجودہ ہزار درہم کی نسبت ( جن کا حکم مدعی اول کے لئے کر دیا تھا) اب بدل کر یوں حکم دیا جائے گا کہ وہ دونوں میں مشترک ہیں۔ کیونکہ اول کے لئے حکم دے دینا دوسرے کا حق باطل نہیں کرتا اس لئے کہ قاضی نے اس کو اپنے اختیار سے اول بنایا تھایا قرعہ اندازی میں اس کا نام پہلے نکل آیا تھا۔ اور ان میں سے کوئی بات ایسی نہیں جو دوسرے کا حق مٹادے پھر اگر وہ ثانی کے لئے قسم کھالے تو شیخ بز دوئی نے اس کا حکم ذکر نہیں کیا۔ البتہ ان کے بھائی ابو اللیث نے کہا ہے فان حلف يقضى بنكوله لِلْأَوَّل ۔
Book of Deposit. So if the holder takes an oath for both, nothing will be for them because no proof is found. And if for the first [؟] the ruling will be given. Because proof... And if the first claimant refuses to take an oath, then a ruling will not be given immediately; rather, an oath will be taken for the second claimant. Contrary to this, if the defendant (the holder) confesses to one of the two claimants, a ruling will be given for the one confessed to, because confession is a proof that is self-operative. So with the confession, a ruling will be given immediately. As for refusal, it is not self-operative; rather, it becomes a proof only when the refusal occurs in the judge's court. Therefore, in the case of refusal, it is permissible to delay the first ruling so that he may take an oath for the second claimant and the method of judgment becomes clear, whether he will decide the thousand for the first claimant or for both of them. Because if the holder also refuses to take an oath for the second, then the thousand will be shared between them both. Hence, delay in judgment. And if the holder also refuses to take an oath for the second claimant, then the thousand will be ruled to be half and half between the two claimants (this is the case mentioned in the book) because in terms of proof, both claimants are equal. Just as if both claimants establish evidence, then this same ruling applies. Also, one thousand dirhams become obligatory on the holder, and they will also be half and half between the two claimants, because his not taking an oath is a confession to both claims. That is, he made a right obligatory upon himself either by way of payment (according to Imam Abu Hanifa) or by way of confession (according to the Sahibayn), and confession is a proof for the confessor's own self. So the right of each of the two claimants became one thousand each, even though he only gave one thousand. So he has paid half of each one's right by means of the other's half right. So he becomes a guarantor for half of each of their rights. This is the ruling according to our scholars. Faqih Abu Layth said in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir that according to Ibn Abi Layla's view, only one thousand would be obligatory on the mentioned holder. His statement: 'Each one's claim is valid...' In Kifayah Sharh Taj al-Shari'ah and Nata'ij al-Afkar, it is said that by validity of the claim is meant validity individually, not collectively. Therefore, the author of al-Hidayah's reasoning 'because it is not necessary that they are truthful' is complete without complication. Sa'di Chalisi interpreted validity of the claims as being valid collectively and strained in explaining the text, saying that both claims are valid collectively, such that one claimant gave a thousand dirhams as a deposit to someone, then the depositee bought some goods from another and deposited that thousand dirhams with him. But according to the author of Nata'ij, this explanation is wrong because in the original issue it is stated that 'two men claimed, each of them that it is his deposit' which indicates that each of them claimed that he is the owner of the thousand and he deposited them. And it is obvious that a single specific thing being wholly owned by two persons simultaneously, and being deposited from both sides, is inconceivable. In the mentioned explanation, the ownership of the holder over the thousand dirhams from one of them had ceased due to the purchase of goods. So how can it be likely that he is truthful in both claims? His statement: 'Because of the difference of rights.' The author of 'Inayah and the author of Binayah and a group of commentators said in the reasoning for the difference of rights: 'because each of them claims a thousand.' But this reasoning is objected to: each claimant is not an absolute claimant of a thousand; rather, he claims the specific thousand dirhams that are in the possession of the defendant, as clarified in the formulation of the issue. And in the chapter on deposits, currency becomes specific, as is established in its place. And 'Allamah Zayla'i has clarified this in Tabyin, where he said: 'Because currency becomes specific in deposits and usurped property.' So the mentioned reasoning does not indicate a difference of rights. Sa'di Chalisi explained the difference of rights on another basis, and that is that the difference of right is due to the difference of the entitled person, because for each claimant there is a right to an oath due to the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him). The author of Nata'ij says that this explanation is useless here because each of them having a right to an oath... Ashraf al-Hidayah, volume eleven. Deposit. They will be divided, with difficulty upon it [?]. (Rather, this requirement is also fulfilled by taking oath from both of them together.) While here the intention is that an oath should be taken for each separately. And the clearest in its reasoning here is what the author of al-Kafi mentioned, who said: 'He swears for each of them separately because each of them claimed separately.' His statement: 'So the method of judgment becomes clear.' The author of 'Inayah, while mentioning three possibilities in explaining the method of judgment, said: 'That judgment be given for the thousand to the first, or to the second, or to both of them.' The author of Nata'ij says that the possibility of the second is wrong because after the holder's refusal of oath for the first, there is no question of judging the thousand for the second. So here only two possibilities exist: either the judge decides the thousand for both, or it becomes clear that it is only for the first. And it is surprising that the author of 'Inayah himself said in his reasoning: 'Because if he swears for the second, there is nothing for him, and if he swears for the first, the whole thousand is for him. And if he also refuses for the second, the thousand is between them.' This reasoning makes it certain that only two possibilities exist here. Actually, the source of the author of 'Inayah's slip is the statement of the commentators in explaining the method of judgment: 'that judgment be given for the thousand to both of them or to one of them.' He understood 'one of them' as general for both first and second, while by 'one of them' they meant only the first claimant. And if the judge gave judgment for the first when the holder refused to take an oath for the first, then Imam Bazdawi's viewpoint regarding the second: 'And if the judge gave judgment for the first when he refused, Imam al-Bazdawi mentioned in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir that an oath will be taken for the second, and if he refuses, judgment will be given between them, because the judgment for the first does not nullify the right of the second, since he gave him priority either by his own choice or by lot, and none of that nullifies the right of the second.' Translation: And if the judge gave judgment for the first when the holder refused to take an oath for the first, Imam Bazdawi mentioned in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir that an oath will also be taken for the second. Now if he refuses, then the existing thousand dirhams will be ruled to be shared between both. Because giving judgment for the first does not invalidate the right of the second, since the judge made him first by his own choice or by lot, and none of these matters invalidate the right of the second. Elucidation: His statement: 'And if the judge gave judgment...' - If the holder refused to take an oath for the first claimant and the judge immediately gave judgment for the first, then Shaykh Bazdawi mentioned in Sharh al-Jami' that (the judgment will not be effective), so an oath will also be taken for the second claimant. If he refuses, then regarding the existing thousand dirhams (which had been judged for the first claimant) the ruling will now be changed such that they are shared between both. Because giving judgment for the first does not nullify the right of the second, since the judge made him first by his own choice or his name came out first in the lottery. And none of these things erase the right of the second. Then if he (the second) takes an oath, Shaykh Bazdawi did not mention its ruling. However, his brother Abu al-Layth said: 'If he swears, judgment will be given based on his refusal (of the first) for the first.'
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on a ruling from a Hanafi fiqh text (likely al-Hidayah) concerning a dispute where two individuals each claim that a specific thousand dirhams held by a depositee (qabid) were deposited by them. The passage covers multiple scenarios and intra-Hanafi disagreements.

The core ruling: If the depositee (qabid) swears an oath for both claimants that he does not owe them, then neither claimant gets anything because no proof is established. If he refuses to swear for the first claimant (nukul), the judge does not immediately rule for the first; instead, he takes an oath from the second claimant. If the qabid also refuses for the second, then the thousand is divided equally between the two claimants. This is because both claimants are equal in terms of proof (both have the same legal status).

An important nuance: If the qabid confesses (iqrar) to one of the claimants, judgment is given immediately for that claimant because confession is a self-operative proof. Refusal (nukul) is not self-operative; it becomes a proof only when it occurs in the judge's court. Hence, the judge delays ruling for the first to see if the second also refuses.

The passage then discusses the liability of the qabid. By refusing to swear for both, he is deemed to have admitted both claims. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, this is like a payment (badl) that creates liability, while according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is like a confession (iqrar). In either case, he becomes liable for one thousand dirhams to be shared between the two claimants. However, since he only has one thousand (the actual deposit), he pays half to each, and the other half is offset because each half pays for the other. This is the Hanafi position. Ibn Abi Layla differed, holding that only one thousand is due (to be divided).

Next, the commentary explains the phrase 'each claimant's claim is valid'. It clarifies that validity means individually, not collectively. A collective validity is impossible because one specific item cannot be owned by two persons simultaneously. The attempt by Sa'di Chalisi to interpret it collectively is rejected.

Then it discusses the reasoning for the difference of rights (taghayur al-haqqain). Some commentators said it is because each claims a thousand, but this is objected to because each claims a specific identified thousand in the qabid's possession, and currency becomes specific in deposits. The correct reasoning is that the difference is due to the difference of the entitled persons: each has the right to an oath. The author of al-Kafi gives the best reasoning: each is sworn separately because each claimed separately.

Finally, the passage discusses the scenario where the judge prematurely rules for the first claimant before taking an oath from the second. According to Imam Bazdawi, such a judgment is not effective; the second claimant must still be given an oath, and if he refuses, the thousand is shared. This is because the judge's prioritization (whether by choice or lot) does not nullify the second's right. If the second swears, Abu al-Layth says the judgment reverts to the first based on the first's refusal.

Throughout, the commentary emphasizes the procedural fairness in a complex dispute where two claimants have equal standing, and the depositee's refusal to swear is treated as an admission creating joint liability.

Key Terms
صحت دعویٰ (sihhat al-da'wa): Validity of the claim; the legal recognition that a claim has a basis to be heard.
تغایر حقین (taghayur al-haqqain): Difference of the two rights; the legal distinction that allows separate treatment of each claimant.
انفراد (infirad): Individuality; considering each claim separately.
اجتماع (ijtima'): Collectivity; the incorrect interpretation that both claims are valid simultaneously.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi commentators, what does it mean that each claimant's claim is 'valid'?
A) Both claims are factually true.
B) Each claim is valid individually, not collectively.
C) Only the first claimant's claim is valid.
D) The claims are valid only if supported by evidence.

Key Takeaway
Each claim is procedurally valid individually; the correct reasoning for separate treatment is that each claimed separately.

Qada — Judiciary
advanced
8 min
Effect of Judge's Ruling After Nukul for First Claimant: Bazdawi vs. Khassaf
Intra-Hanafi dispute on effect of judgment after nukul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two Hanafi positions on the effect of a judge's ruling after nukul for the first claimant and explain the reasoning of each, including the sub-dispute between Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf on the modified oath.

Core Idea
A judge's ruling for one claimant after nukul does not always extinguish the other's right — the Hanafi school is divided on finality.

This passage delves into an intra-Hanafi debate about the consequences of a judicial ruling after the custodian's refusal to take an oath (nukul). When two claimants each claim the same deposited property, and the judge rules for the first claimant after the custodian's nukul, what are the second claimant's rights? The Hanafi scholars al-Bazdawi and al-Khassaf offer contrasting views, revealing the nuanced interplay between judicial finality and the probative value of nukul. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to trace how later Hanafi authorities build upon the foundational positions of the Sahibayn.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and the legal question
Understand the facts: two claimants each claim the same deposited property (e.g., a slave). The custodian refuses to take an oath for the first claimant, and the judge rules in favour of the first. The key question is: does the second claimant retain any right to demand an oath or a share?
The nukul is central — it is not an admission but a refusal that can ground a ruling.
2
Identify Imam al-Bazdawi's position and reasoning
Bazdawi holds that the judgment for the first does not invalidate the second's right. The second can still demand an oath from the custodian; if again refused, the property is shared equally. His reasoning: the judge's selection of the first (by choice or lot) is procedural and does not conclusively establish the first's ownership.
Bazdawi's view treats the first ruling as provisional.
3
Identify Imam al-Khassaf's position and reasoning
Khassaf holds the judgment is immediately enforceable (nafidh). He places the case concerning a slave. The nukul is a circumstantial acknowledgment (dalalat al-iqrar), making the ruling final because it falls within a sphere of ijtihad. Consequently, the second cannot claim ownership of the slave.
Khassaf's view treats nukul as effectively equivalent to an admission in this context.
4
Analyse the sub-dispute on the modified oath
Within Khassaf's view, there is further disagreement between Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf. The question: should the custodian be made to swear a modified oath that the second has no right to the slave's value? Imam Muhammad says yes, because the underlying rule makes the depositor liable for the value after the property is awarded to another. Abu Yusuf disagrees, as he does not hold the depositor liable. This sub-dispute is a branch (fari'ah) of that underlying issue.
This shows how subsidiary rulings often depend on principles in related chapters.
5
Synthesize the outcome and authority weight
Both positions are recorded in later Hanafi works. The passage acknowledges prolixity (itnab) and leaves no single mufta bihi. The authority weight is nawadir (rare transmissions) as these are views of later commentators, not the six core books.
In fatwa practice, a judge may follow either view depending on the situation, as both are within the scope of ijtihad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ قَضَى الْقَاضِي لِلْأَوَّلِ حِينَ نَكَلَ ذَكَرَ الْإِمَامُ الْبَزْدَوِيُّ فِي شَرْحِ الْجَامِعِ الصَّغِيرِ أَنَّهُ يُحَلَّفُ لِلثَّانِي فَإِذَا نَكَلَ يُقْضَى بَيْنَهُمَا لِأَنَّ الْقَضَاءَ لِلْأَوَّلِ لَا يُبْطِلُ حَقَّ الثَّانِي لِأَنَّهُ يُقَدِّمُهُ إِمَّا بِنَفْسِهِ أَوْ بِالْقُرْعَةِ وَكُلُّ ذَلِكَ لَا يُبْطِلُ حَقَّ الثَّانِي. وَذَكَرَ الْخَصَّافُ أَنَّهُ نَفَذَ قَضَاؤُهُ لِلْأَوَّلِ وَوَضَعَ الْمَسْأَلَةَ فِي الْعَبْدِ وَإِنَّمَا نَفَذَ لِمُصَادَفَتِهِ مَحَلَّ الِاجْتِهَادِ لِأَنَّ مِنَ الْعُلَمَاءِ مَنْ قَالَ يَقْضِي لِلْأَوَّلِ وَلَا يَنْتَظِرُ لِكَوْنِهِ إِقْرَارًا دَلَالَةً ثُمَّ لَا يَحْلِفُ لِلثَّانِي مَا هَذَا الْعَبْدُ لِي لِأَنَّ نُكُولَهُ لَا يُفِيدُ بَعْدَمَا صَارَ لِلْأَوَّلِ. وَهَلْ يُحَلِّفُهُ بِاللَّهِ مَا لِهَذَا عَلَيْكَ هَذَا الْعَبْدُ وَلَا قِيمَتُهُ وَهُوَ كَذَا وَكَذَا وَلَا أَقَلُّ مِنْهُ؟ قَالَ يَنْبَغِي أَنْ يُحَلَّفَهُ عِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ خِلَافًا لِأَبِي يُوسُفَ بِنَاءً عَلَى أَنَّ الْمُودِعَ إِذَا أَقَرَّ بِالْوَدِيعَةِ وَدُفِعَ بِالْقَضَاءِ إِلَى غَيْرِهِ يَضْمَنُهُ عِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ خِلَافًا لَهُ. وَهَذِهِ فَرِيعَةُ تِلْكَ الْمَسْأَلَةِ وَقَدْ وَقَعَ فِيهَا بَعْضُ الْإِطْنَابِ وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ.
And if the judge ruled for the first when he (the custodian) refused the oath, Imam al-Bazdawi mentioned in his commentary on al-Jami' al-Saghir that he is made to take an oath for the second, and if he refuses, it is ruled between them (i.e., the property is shared), because the ruling for the first does not invalidate the right of the second, since he (the judge) gave him precedence either by his own choice or by lot, and all of that does not invalidate the right of the second. And al-Khassaf mentioned that his ruling for the first is effective, and he placed the issue concerning a slave, and it is only effective because it coincides with a place of ijtihad, since some scholars say he should rule for the first and not wait, because it is an indication of acknowledgment. Then he does not administer an oath for the second (saying) 'This slave is mine' because his refusal (to take the oath) is of no benefit after it (the slave) has become for the first. And should he administer an oath to him by Allah: 'This claimant has no right to this slave from you, nor its value, which is such-and-such, nor less than that?' He said: It is proper to administer the oath according to Muhammad, contrary to Abu Yusuf, based on the fact that when the depositor acknowledges the deposit and it is handed over by judicial order to someone else, he is guarantor for it according to Muhammad, contrary to him (Abu Yusuf). And this is a branch of that issue, and there has occurred some prolixity in it, and Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the effect of a judge's ruling for the first claimant after the custodian's refusal to take an oath (nukul) when two claimants each claim the same deposited property. Imam al-Bazdawi states that the ruling for the first does not immediately finalize the matter; the second claimant still has the right to demand an oath from the custodian. If the custodian again refuses, the judge rules that the property is shared between the two claimants. Bazdawi's reasoning is that the judge's initial selection of the first claimant (whether by his own choice or by lot) does not invalidate the second claimant's right. On the other hand, Imam al-Khassaf holds that the judge's ruling for the first is immediately enforceable (nafidh). He places the issue in the context of a slave rather than money. The ruling is effective because it falls within a sphere of ijtihad (mujtahid fih), since some scholars opine that the judge should rule immediately for the first without waiting, because the custodian's refusal to take the oath is a circumstantial acknowledgment (dalalat al-iqrar). Consequently, the second claimant does not receive a simple ownership oath ('This slave is mine') because after the slave has been awarded to the first, such an oath would be futile. Instead, a modified oath is considered: the custodian swears that the second claimant has no right to the slave itself nor its value (minimum or specific amount). According to Imam Muhammad, this modified oath should be administered, but Abu Yusuf disagrees. The basis of this sub-dispute is a related issue: when a depositor acknowledges a deposit and then, by court order, it is given to someone else, Imam Muhammad holds the depositor becomes liable (dhamin) for it, while Abu Yusuf does not. Thus, this question of the oath for the second claimant is a branch (fari'ah) of that foundational issue. The passage notes some prolixity (itnab) in this discussion.

Key Terms
نُكُول (nukūl): Refusal of a party to take a sworn oath (yamīn) when required by the court, which in some cases gives the judge discretion to rule against the refuser.
دَلالَةُ الإقْرَار (dalālatu al-iqrār): A circumstantial indication that the party is effectively acknowledging the claim, here the custodian's refusal to take an oath implying the claim is true.
مَحَلُّ الإجْتِهَاد (maḥallu al-ijtihād): A matter open to independent legal reasoning because primary texts do not provide a decisive ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam al-Khassaf, what is the status of the second claimant's right to take an oath regarding ownership of the slave after the judge's ruling for the first claimant?
A) The second claimant still demands the same ownership oath as before.
B) The second claimant gets a limited oath about the slave's value but not ownership.
C) The second claimant's right is completely extinguished.
D) The second claimant must produce witnesses instead.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school contains two distinct positions on the finality of a judge's ruling after nukul, and even within the position of finality, there is further disagreement on whether a value oath is available to the second claimant.
